BlueprintArchitectMulti-VM complex deployments with dependenciesЩҶЩҺШҙШұ Щ…ЩҸШ№ЩҺЩӮЩҺЩ‘ШҜ

IaaS Self-Service Console

📚 IaaS Console Features
  • ЩҶЩҺШҙШұ VMs Щ…ЩҺШ№ ШӘЩҺШ®ШөЩҠШө ЩғШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„ (CPU, RAM, Disk, Network)
  • Ш§ЩҗШ®ШӘЩҠШ§Шұ VM Class ЩҲЩҺ Storage Class
  • ШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ VPC Subnet ЩҲЩҺШ№ЩҸЩҶЩҲШ§ЩҶ IP
  • ШҘЩҗШ¶Ш§ЩҒШ© Cloud-Init / Guest Customization scripts
  • ШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ Placement preferences

ШҜЩҺЩҲШұШ© ШӯЩҺЩҠШ§Ш© Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ШҙШұ вҖ” Deployment Lifecycle

PhaseStateActionsШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎШ§ШӘ
1RequestedPending approval (if policy)ШЁЩҗШ§ЩҗЩҶШӘЩҗШёШ§Шұ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩҲШ§ЩҒЩҺЩӮШ©
2ProvisioningResources allocatedШӘЩҺШ®ШөЩҠШө Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ
3ActivePower, Snapshot, Resize, ReconfigureШӘЩҺШҙШәЩҠЩ„ШҢ Щ„ЩҺЩӮШ·Ш©ШҢ ШӘЩҺШәЩҠЩҠШұ
4Lease ExpiringExtend or destroyШӘЩҺЩ…ШҜЩҠШҜ ШЈЩҺЩҲ ШӯЩҺШ°ЩҒ
5DestroyedResources releasedШӘЩҺШӯШұЩҠШұ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ

Day-2 Operations вҖ” Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ Щ…Ш§ ШЁЩҺШ№ШҜ Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ШҙШұ

🧠 Day-2 Actions

  • Power Operations: Power On, Off, Restart, Suspend
  • Snapshot: Create, Revert, Delete
  • Resize: Change CPU/Memory
  • Add Disk: Attach additional storage
  • Reconfigure Network: Change NIC/subnet
  • Remote Console: Web-based access
  • Guest OS Ops: Reboot, change password
  • Delete/Destroy: Remove and release resources

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What does VM Service allow?

Correct: B

VM Service enables deploying VMs through the Kubernetes API, bridging traditional and modern approaches.

Q2. What is a Supervisor Cluster?

Correct: B

The Supervisor Cluster is the Kubernetes management layer integrated into vSphere.

Q3. Which databases does Data Services Manager support?

Correct: B

Data Services Manager supports PostgreSQL, MySQL, Redis, and RabbitMQ.

Q4. What are Namespace Classes?

Correct: B

Namespace Classes are templates that define resource quotas and policies for Kubernetes namespaces.

Module 13 · VCF Operations Overview

ЩҶЩҺШёШұШ© Ш№Ш§Щ…Щ‘Ш© Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү VCF Operations

VCF Operations Overview

VCF Operations ЩҠЩҸЩҲЩҺЩҒЩҗЩ‘Шұ ШұЩҸШӨЩҠШ© ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш© Щ„ЩҗШөЩҗШӯЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҗЩҶЩҠШ© Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯШӘЩҠЩ‘Ш© ЩҲЩҺШЈЩҺШҜШ§ШҰЩҮШ§ ЩҲЩҺШіЩҺШ№ЩҺШӘЩҮШ§ Ш№ЩҺШЁШұ ШЈЩҺШҜЩҲШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„.

Learning Objectives
  • ЩҒЩҺЩҮЩ… ШЁЩҗЩҶЩҠШ© VCF Operations ЩҲЩҺЩ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘЩҮШ§
  • Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶЩҺЩӮЩҸЩ‘Щ„ ЩҒЩҠ ЩҲШ§Ш¬ЩҗЩҮШ© VCF Operations
  • ЩҲЩҺШөЩҒ ШҜЩҺЩҲШұШ© Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ (Collection вҶ’ Analysis вҶ’ Visualization)

Щ…Ш§ ЩҮЩҲ VCF Operations?

  • Щ…ЩҺЩҶШөЩ‘Ш© Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© ЩҲЩҺШӘЩҺШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„ ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ VCF
  • ШӘЩҺШ¬Щ…ЩҺШ№ metrics Щ…ЩҗЩҶ: vCenter, ESXi, NSX, vSAN
  • ШӘЩҺШіШӘЩҺШ®ШҜЩҗЩ… Machine Learning Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶЩҺШЁЩҸЩ‘ШӨ ЩҲЩҺШ§ЩғШӘЩҗШҙШ§ЩҒ Ш§Щ„ШҙЩҸЩ‘Ш°ЩҲШ°
  • ШӘЩҸЩӮЩҺШҜЩҗЩ‘Щ… ШӘЩҲШөЩҠШ§ШӘ Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШЁШ§ЩӮЩҠЩ‘Ш© Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺШӯШіЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШҜШ§ШЎ

Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШұЩҺЩ‘ШҰЩҠШіЩҠЩ‘Ш©

ComponentFunctionШ§Щ„ЩҲЩҺШёЩҠЩҒШ©
Analytics ClusterData collection, ML processing, alertingШ¬ЩҺЩ…Ш№ Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘШҢ Щ…ЩҸШ№Ш§Щ„ЩҺШ¬Ш© MLШҢ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ
Collector NodesRemote collection from data sourcesШ¬ЩҺЩ…Ш№ Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҗЩҶ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШөШ§ШҜЩҗШұ Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺШ№ЩҠШҜШ©
Management PacksExtend monitoring to 3rd-party systemsШӘЩҺЩҲШіЩҠШ№ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Щ„ЩҗШЈЩҺЩҶШёЩҗЩ…Ш© Ш®Ш§ШұЩҗШ¬ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

ШЁЩҗЩҶЩҠШ© VCF Operations вҖ” Architecture Details

Node TypeRoleШ§Щ„ШҜЩҺЩ‘ЩҲШұ
Primary NodeAnalytics engine, configuration, UIЩ…ЩҸШӯЩҺШұЩҗЩ‘Щғ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„Ш§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ЩҲШ§Ш¬ЩҗЩҮШ©
Primary ReplicaHA failover for PrimaryШ§ЩҗШӯШӘЩҗЩҠШ§Ш·ЩҠ Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШЈЩҺШіШ§ШіЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©
Data NodeTime-series metric storage, horizontal scalingШӘЩҺШ®ШІЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі
Collector NodeRemote metric collection from adaptersШ¬ЩҺЩ…Ш№ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі Ш№ЩҺЩҶ ШЁЩҸШ№ШҜ

Multinode Cluster Sizing

⚠️ Cluster Sizing Guide
SizeNodesObjectsШ§Щ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶШ§ШӘ
Small2 (1P + 1R)Up to 4,000ШӯЩҺШӘЩ‘Щү 4,000
Medium4 (1P + 1R + 2D)Up to 15,000ШӯЩҺШӘЩ‘Щү 15,000
Large8+ (1P + 1R + 6+D)Up to 70,000+ШӯЩҺШӘЩ‘Щү 70,000+

Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„Ш§ШӘ вҖ” Analytics Capabilities

🧠 Key Capabilities

  • Predictive Analytics: ШӘЩҺЩҶЩҺШЁЩҸЩ‘ШӨ ШЁЩҗШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШҙШ§ЩғЩҗЩ„ ЩӮЩҺШЁЩ„ ШӯЩҸШҜЩҲШ«ЩҮШ§
  • Root Cause Analysis: ШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺШЁ Ш§Щ„Ш¬ЩҗШ°ШұЩҠ ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш§ЩӢ
  • Capacity Planning: Щ…ЩҺШӘЩү ЩҶЩҺШӯШӘШ§Ш¬ Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ ШҘЩҗШ¶Ш§ЩҒЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©Шҹ
  • Optimization: ШӘЩҺЩҲШөЩҗЩҠШ§ШӘ Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺШӯШіЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШҜШ§ШЎ
  • Compliance: ЩҒЩҺШӯШө Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗЩ…ШӘЩҗШ«Ш§Щ„ (CIS, DISA STIG)
  • Cost Analysis: ШӘЩҺШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩғШ§Щ„ЩҠЩҒ

Adapters вҖ” Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШӯЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘Щ„Ш§ШӘ

AdapterData CollectedШ§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ
vCenterVMs, Hosts, Clusters, DatastoresЩ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ
NSXSegments, firewall rules, load balancersШ§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩғШ§ШӘ
vSANStorage performance, capacity, healthШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ
SDDC HealthOverall VCF health and complianceШ§Щ„ШөЩҗЩ‘ШӯЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ШҙЩ‘Ш§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш©

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What technology does VCF Operations use for anomaly detection?

Correct: B

VCF Operations uses Machine Learning for predictive analytics and anomaly detection.

Q2. What are Management Packs?

Correct: B

Management Packs extend VCF Operations' monitoring to third-party systems and services.

Q3. What data sources does VCF Operations collect from?

Correct: B

VCF Operations collects metrics from vCenter, ESXi hosts, NSX, and vSAN.

Module 14 · Metrics and Objects

Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶШ§ШӘ

Metrics and Objects

ЩҒЩҺЩҮЩ… ЩғЩҺЩҠЩҒЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш¬ЩҺЩ…Ш№ ЩҲЩҺШӘЩҺЩҶШёЩҠЩ… Metrics ЩҲЩҺObjects ЩҮЩҲ ШЈЩҺШіШ§Ші Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„ Ш§Щ„ЩҒЩҺШ№Щ‘Ш§Щ„ ЩҒЩҠ VCF Operations.

Learning Objectives
  • Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Щ…ЩҠЩҠШІ ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ Object Types ЩҲЩҺ Metrics
  • ЩҒЩҺЩҮЩ… Dynamic Thresholds vs Static Thresholds
  • Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ®ШҜШ§Щ… Super Metrics

Objects ЩҲЩҺ Metrics

ConceptDefinitionШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш№ШұЩҠЩҒ
ObjectA monitored entity (VM, Host, Cluster, Datastore)ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶ Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁ
MetricA measurable property of an object (CPU %, mem usage)Ш®Ш§ШөЩҗЩ‘ЩҠЩ‘Ш© ЩӮШ§ШЁЩҗЩ„Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩ„ЩӮЩҗЩҠШ§Ші
PropertyA static attribute (name, OS type, power state)ШөЩҗЩҒШ© Ш«Ш§ШЁЩҗШӘШ©
Super MetricCustom formula combining multiple metricsШөЩҠШәШ© Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘ШөШ© ШӘЩҺШ¬Щ…ЩҺШ№ Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі Щ…ЩҸШӘЩҺШ№ЩҺШҜЩҗЩ‘ШҜШ©

Dynamic Thresholds

⚠️ Dynamic vs Static Thresholds
  • Static: ЩӮЩҗЩҠЩ…Ш© Ш«Ш§ШЁЩҗШӘШ© (Щ…ЩҺШ«ЩҺЩ„Ш§ЩӢ: CPU > 90% = alert)
  • Dynamic: ML ЩҠЩҺШӘЩҺШ№ЩҺЩ„ЩҺЩ‘Щ… Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘Щ…ЩҺШ· Ш§Щ„Ш·ЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҠШ№ЩҠ ЩҲЩҺЩҠЩҸЩҶЩҺШЁЩҗЩ‘ЩҮ Ш№ЩҗЩҶШҜ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗЩҶШӯЩҗШұШ§ЩҒ
  • VCF Operations ЩҠЩҺШіШӘЩҺШ®ШҜЩҗЩ… Dynamic Thresholds ШЁЩҗШҙЩҺЩғЩ„ Ш§ЩҗЩҒШӘЩҗШұШ§Ш¶ЩҠ
  • ЩҠЩҺШӯШӘШ§Ш¬ ~2 ШЈЩҸШіШЁЩҲШ№ЩҺЩҠЩҶ Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺШ№ЩҺЩ„ЩҸЩ‘Щ… Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺЩҶЩ…Ш§Ш· Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШіШ§ШіЩҠЩ‘Ш©

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі вҖ” Metric Types

CategoryExamplesШЈЩҺЩ…Ш«ЩҗЩ„Ш©
PerformanceCPU %, Memory Active, Disk LatencyШ§Щ„ШЈЩҺШҜШ§ШЎ
CapacityRemaining Time, Time to Full, ReclaimableШ§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш№Ш©
HealthHealth Score, Anomaly Count, Active AlertsШ§Щ„ШөЩҗЩ‘ШӯЩ‘Ш©
ConfigurationvCPU count, Memory Size, Disk SizeШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҸШұЩҲШ¶ вҖ” View Types

View TypeDescriptionШ§Щ„ЩҲЩҺШөЩҒ
List ViewTabular display of objects with metricsШ№ЩҺШұШ¶ Ш¬ЩҺШҜЩҲЩҺЩ„ЩҠ
Summary ViewAggregated statistics for a groupШҘЩҗШӯШөШ§ШҰЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ Щ…ЩҸШ¬ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ‘Ш№Ш©
Trend ViewTime-series graph of metric changesШұЩҺШіЩ… ШІЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩҶЩҠ
Distribution ViewHistogram of metric across objectsШӘЩҺЩҲШІЩҠШ№ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі

ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Ш№ЩҺШұШ¶ Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘Шө вҖ” Custom View Creation

  1. Visualize вҶ’ Views вҶ’ CREATE
  2. Ш§ЩҗШ®ШӘЩҠШ§Шұ ЩҶЩҺЩҲШ№ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҺШұШ¶ ЩҲЩҺ Object Type
  3. ШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ (Metrics, Properties, Alerts)
  4. ШҘЩҗШ¶Ш§ЩҒШ© Filter Щ„ЩҗЩ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶШ§ШӘ
  5. Щ…ЩҸШ№Ш§ЩҠЩҶШ© Live Data вҶ’ ШӯЩҗЩҒШё

Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩӮШ§ШұЩҠШұ вҖ” Reports

🧠 Report Features

  • Scheduled: ЩҠЩҺЩҲЩ…ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©ШҢ ШЈЩҸШіШЁЩҲШ№ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©ШҢ ШҙЩҺЩҮШұЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©
  • On-Demand: ЩҒЩҺЩҲШұЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш№ЩҗЩҶШҜ Ш§Щ„Ш·ЩҺЩ‘Щ„ЩҺШЁ
  • Templates: ЩӮЩҺЩҲШ§Щ„ЩҗШЁ Ш¬Ш§ЩҮЩҗШІШ© ЩӮШ§ШЁЩҗЩ„Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШөЩҠШө
  • Export: PDF, CSV
  • Email Delivery: ШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҠ

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What is a Super Metric?

Correct: B

A Super Metric is a user-defined formula that combines multiple metrics for custom analysis.

Q2. How long does VCF Operations need to learn baseline patterns?

Correct: B

VCF Operations needs approximately 2 weeks to learn normal baseline patterns using ML.

Q3. What is the difference between a Metric and a Property?

Correct: B

Metrics are measurable, time-varying properties (CPU%, memory), while Properties are static attributes (name, OS).

Module 15 · Dashboards and Views

Щ„ЩҺЩҲШӯШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШ№Щ„ЩҲЩ…Ш§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Ш№ЩҸШұЩҲШ¶

Dashboards and Views

Dashboards ШӘЩҸЩӮЩҺШҜЩҗЩ‘Щ… ШұЩҸШӨЩҠШ© ШЁЩҺШөЩҺШұЩҠЩ‘Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘШҢ ЩҲЩҺViews ШӘЩҸЩ…ЩҺЩғЩҗЩ‘ЩҶ Щ…ЩҗЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҸЩ‘ЩӮ ЩҒЩҠ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҒШ§ШөЩҠЩ„.

Learning Objectives
  • ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Dashboards Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘ШөШ©
  • Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ®ШҜШ§Щ… Views ЩҲЩҺ Reports
  • ШЁЩҗЩҶШ§ШЎ ШӘЩҺЩӮШ§ШұЩҠШұ Щ…ЩҸШ¬ЩҺШҜЩҲЩҺЩ„Ш©

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Dashboards

  • Pre-built Dashboards: Щ„ЩҺЩҲШӯШ§ШӘ Ш¬Ш§ЩҮЩҗШІШ© (Overview, Capacity, Performance)
  • Custom Dashboards: Щ„ЩҺЩҲШӯШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘ШөШ© ШЁЩҗЩҖ widgets ЩӮШ§ШЁЩҗЩ„Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШіЩҺЩ‘ШӯШЁ
  • Widgets: Chart, Scoreboard, Top-N, Heat Map, Weather Map, Topology
  • Interactions: Ш§Щ„ШұЩҺЩ‘ШЁШ· ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ widgets вҖ” Ш§ЩҗШ®ШӘЩҠШ§Шұ ЩҒЩҠ widget ЩҠЩҸШӯЩҺШҜЩҗЩ‘Ш« Ш§Щ„ШўШ®ЩҺШұЩҠЩҶ

Views ЩҲЩҺ Reports

FeatureUse CaseШ§Щ„Ш§ШіШӘЩҗШ®ШҜШ§Щ…
ViewsTabular data exploration with filtersШ§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗЩғШҙШ§ЩҒ Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ ШЁЩҗЩҒЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҗШұШ§ШӘ
ReportsScheduled PDF/CSV exportsШӘЩҺЩӮШ§ШұЩҠШұ Щ…ЩҸШ¬ЩҺШҜЩҲЩҺЩ„Ш© PDF/CSV
Object RelationsTopology and dependency mapsШ®ЩҺШұШ§ШҰЩҗШ· Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ„Ш§ЩӮШ§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШ№ШӘЩҗЩ…Ш§ШҜЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ
🔬 Lab 21: Creating Dashboards

ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Dashboard Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘Шө Щ…ЩҺШ№ widgets Щ„ЩҗЩ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШҜШ§ШЎ.

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Widgets вҖ” Widget Types

WidgetPurposeШ§Щ„ШәЩҺШұЩҺШ¶
Metric ChartLine/area chart over timeШұЩҺШіЩ… ШІЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩҶЩҠ
ScoreboardKey metric cards at a glanceШЁЩҗШ·Ш§ЩӮШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі
Heat MapColor-coded metric density gridШҙЩҺШЁЩҺЩғШ© Щ…ЩҸЩ„ЩҺЩҲЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШ©
Top-NTop/Bottom N objects by metricШЈЩҺШ№Щ„Щү/ШЈЩҺШҜЩҶЩү N
Alert ListActive alerts for objectsШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ШҙЩҗШ·Ш©
Object ListFiltered objects with statusЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҺШ№ Ш§Щ„ШӯШ§Щ„Ш©
TopologyRelationship mapШ®ЩҺШұЩҠШ·Ш© Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ„Ш§ЩӮШ§ШӘ
View WidgetEmbeds saved ViewЩҠЩҺШҜЩ…ЩҸШ¬ Ш№ЩҺШұШ¶ Щ…ЩҺШӯЩҒЩҲШё

ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Щ„ЩҺЩҲШӯШ© Щ…ЩҺШ№Щ„ЩҲЩ…Ш§ШӘ вҖ” Creating a Dashboard

  1. Visualize вҶ’ Dashboards вҶ’ CREATE
  2. ШӘЩҺШіЩ…ЩҠШ© Ш§Щ„Щ„ЩҺЩ‘ЩҲШӯШ©
  3. ШҘЩҗШ¶Ш§ЩҒШ© Widgets ШЁЩҗШ§Щ„ШіЩҺЩ‘ШӯШЁ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗЩҒЩ„Ш§ШӘ
  4. ШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Widget (Object Type, Metric, Filter, Time Range)
  5. ШӘЩҺШұШӘЩҠШЁ Layout вҶ’ ШӯЩҗЩҒШё ЩҲЩҺЩ…ЩҸШҙШ§ШұЩҺЩғШ©

ШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© Ш§Щ„Щ„ЩҺЩ‘ЩҲШӯШ§ШӘ вҖ” Dashboard Management

🧠 Management Options

  • Share: Щ…ЩҸШҙШ§ШұЩҺЩғШ© Щ…ЩҺШ№ Щ…ЩҸШіШӘЩҺШ®ШҜЩҗЩ…ЩҠЩҶ/Щ…ЩҺШ¬Щ…ЩҲШ№Ш§ШӘ
  • Clone: ЩҶЩҺШіШ® ЩғЩҺШЈЩҺШіШ§Ші Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺШ№ШҜЩҠЩ„
  • Export/Import: ЩҶЩҺЩӮЩ„ ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ ШЁЩҺЩҠШҰШ§ШӘ
  • Auto-Refresh: ЩғЩҸЩ„Щ‘ 5/15/30 ШҜЩҺЩӮЩҠЩӮШ©
  • Favorites: ШӘЩҺШ«ШЁЩҠШӘ Щ„ЩҗЩ„ЩҲЩҸШөЩҲЩ„ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҺЩ‘ШұЩҠШ№

ШЈЩҺЩҒШ¶ЩҺЩ„ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩ…Ш§ШұЩҺШіШ§ШӘ вҖ” NOC Dashboard Best Practices

💡 Design Tips
  • Scoreboard Щ„ЩҗЩ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі Ш§Щ„ШӯЩҺШұЩҗШ¬Ш© ЩҒЩҠ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШ№Щ„Щү
  • Alert List ШЁЩҗЩҒЩҗЩ„ШӘШұ Critical + Immediate
  • Heat Map Щ„ЩҗШұЩҸШӨЩҠШ© ШіЩҺШұЩҠШ№Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШӯШ§Щ„Ш© Ш§Щ„Ш№Ш§Щ…Щ‘Ш©
  • Auto-refresh ЩғЩҸЩ„Щ‘ 5 ШҜЩҺЩӮШ§ШҰЩҗЩӮ Щ„ЩҗЩ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш§Щ„ШӯЩҺЩҠЩ‘Ш©
  • Щ„ЩҺЩҲШӯШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҸЩҶЩҒЩҺШөЩҗЩ„Ш©: Overview вҶ’ Detail вҶ’ Troubleshooting

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What are Widgets in a Dashboard?

Correct: B

Widgets are visual components (charts, scorecards, heat maps) that display specific metrics data.

Q2. What format can scheduled Reports export?

Correct: B

Reports can be exported as PDF or CSV on a schedule.

Q3. What are Widget Interactions?

Correct: B

Widget Interactions connect widgets so that a selection in one updates the display in linked widgets.

Module 16 · Policies in VCF Operations

Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ ЩҒЩҠ VCF Operations

Policies in VCF Operations

Policies ШӘЩҸШӯЩҺШҜЩҗЩ‘ШҜ ШіЩҸЩ„ЩҲЩғ VCF Operations: Щ…Ш§ ЩҠЩҸШ¬Щ…ЩҺШ№ШҢ ЩғЩҺЩҠЩҒ ЩҠЩҸШӯЩҺЩ„ЩҺЩ‘Щ„ШҢ ЩҲЩҺЩ…ЩҺШӘЩү ЩҠЩҸЩҶЩҺШЁЩҺЩ‘ЩҮ.

Learning Objectives
  • ЩҒЩҺЩҮЩ… ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШӘЩҺШЈШ«ЩҠШұЩҮШ§
  • ШӘЩҺШ№ШҜЩҠЩ„ ЩҲЩҺШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ ШіЩҗЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘ШөШ©
  • ЩҒЩҺЩҮЩ… ШЈЩҺЩҲЩ„ЩҺЩҲЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ вҖ” Policy Types

Policy TypeControlsЩҠЩҺШӘЩҺШӯЩҺЩғЩҺЩ‘Щ… ЩҒЩҠ
Capacity/AllocationWhen is an object "full"?Щ…ЩҺШӘЩү ЩҠЩҺЩғЩҲЩҶ Ш§Щ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶ "Щ…ЩҸЩ…ШӘЩҺЩ„ЩҗШҰ"?
ComplianceConfiguration drift from baselineШ§Щ„Ш§ЩҗЩҶШӯЩҗШұШ§ЩҒ Ш№ЩҺЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШұШ¬ЩҗШ№ЩҠ
WorkloadOver/under utilization rangesЩҶЩҗШ·Ш§ЩӮШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ®ШҜШ§Щ… Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШЁЩҲЩ„Ш©
AutomationWhen to trigger DRS/DPMЩ…ЩҺШӘЩү ЩҠЩҺШ№Щ…ЩҺЩ„ DRS/DPM

ШЈЩҺЩҲЩ„ЩҺЩҲЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ

🧠 Policy Priority (ШЈЩҺШ№Щ„Щү вҶ’ ШЈЩҺШҜЩҶЩү)

  1. Custom Policy on Object: ШЈЩҺШ№Щ„Щү ШЈЩҺЩҲЩ„ЩҺЩҲЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© вҖ” Щ…ЩҸШ·ЩҺШЁЩҺЩ‘ЩӮШ© Щ…ЩҸШЁШ§ШҙЩҺШұШ©ЩӢ
  2. Custom Policy on Group: Щ…ЩҸШ·ЩҺШЁЩҺЩ‘ЩӮШ© Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү Щ…ЩҺШ¬Щ…ЩҲШ№Ш©
  3. Object Type Default: Ш§ЩҗЩҒШӘЩҗШұШ§Ш¶ЩҠ Щ„ЩҗЩҶЩҺЩҲШ№ Ш§Щ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶ
  4. Global Default: ШЈЩҺШҜЩҶЩү ШЈЩҺЩҲЩ„ЩҺЩҲЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© вҖ” Щ…ЩҸШ·ЩҺШЁЩҺЩ‘ЩӮ Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү Ш§Щ„Ш¬ЩҺЩ…ЩҠШ№

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҒШөЩҠЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш© вҖ” Policy Types

Policy TypeScopePurposeШ§Щ„ШәЩҺШұЩҺШ¶
OperationalVMs, Hosts, ClustersThresholds, alert behavior, data collectionШ§Щ„Ш№ЩҺШӘЩҺШЁШ§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШіЩҸЩ„ЩҲЩғ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ
ComplianceVMs, HostsSecurity benchmarks (CIS, DISA)Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШ№Ш§ЩҠЩҠШұ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺЩ…ЩҶЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©
CostVMs, ProjectsCost rates for CPU, Memory, StorageЩ…ЩҸШ№ЩҺШҜЩҺЩ‘Щ„Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩғЩ„ЩҗЩҒШ©
AutomationVMsAuto-remediation on alert triggersШҘЩҗШөЩ„Ш§Шӯ ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҠ

Operational Policies вҖ” Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҒШ§ШөЩҠЩ„

🧠 Policy Configuration

  • Scope: Object Groups, Tags, Custom groups
  • Thresholds: ШӘЩҺШ¬Ш§ЩҲЩҸШІ default Щ„ЩҗЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҸШӯЩҺШҜЩҺЩ‘ШҜШ©
  • Symptoms: ШӘЩҺЩҒШ№ЩҠЩ„/ШӘЩҺШ№Ш·ЩҠЩ„ ШЈЩҺШ№ШұШ§Ш¶ Щ…ЩҸШӯЩҺШҜЩҺЩ‘ШҜШ©
  • Collection Interval: 1/5/15 ШҜЩҺЩӮЩҠЩӮШ©
  • Retention: Щ…ЩҸШҜЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШӯШӘЩҗЩҒШ§Шё ШЁЩҗШ§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ
  • Priority: Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺЩҲЩ„ЩҲЩҠШ© Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШ№Щ„Щү ШӘЩҺШіЩҲШҜ

Compliance Benchmarks вҖ” Щ…ЩҺШ№Ш§ЩҠЩҠШұ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗЩ…ШӘЩҗШ«Ш§Щ„

BenchmarkScopeШ§Щ„ЩҶЩҗЩ‘Ш·Ш§ЩӮ
CIS VMware ESXiHost hardeningШӘЩҺЩӮЩҲЩҠШ© Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШ¶ЩҠЩҒШ§ШӘ
DISA STIG vSphereDoD security guideШҜЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ„ ШЈЩҺЩ…Ш§ЩҶ DoD
VMware Security GuideVMware best practicesШЈЩҺЩҒШ¶ЩҺЩ„ Щ…ЩҸЩ…Ш§ШұЩҺШіШ§ШӘ VMware
Custom BenchmarkOrganization-specific rulesЩӮЩҺЩҲШ§Ш№ЩҗШҜ Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘ШөШ©

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What does a Capacity Policy define?

Correct: B

Capacity Policies define when an object (cluster, datastore) is considered full.

Q2. Which policy has the highest priority?

Correct: C

Custom Policy applied directly to an object has the highest priority.

Q3. What does a Compliance Policy detect?

Correct: B

Compliance Policies detect when object configurations drift from a defined baseline.

Module 17 · Symptoms, Alerts, and Actions

Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШ№ШұШ§Ш¶ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎШ§ШӘ

Symptoms, Alerts, and Actions

ЩҶЩҗШёШ§Щ… Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШӘЩҺЩӮЩҺШҜЩҗЩ‘Щ… ЩҠЩҺШЁШҜЩҺШЈ ШЁЩҗЩҖ SymptomsШҢ ЩҠЩҸЩҶШҙЩҗШҰ AlertsШҢ ЩҲЩҺЩҠЩҸЩҶЩҺЩҒЩҗЩ‘Ш° Actions ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш§ЩӢ.

Learning Objectives
  • Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Щ…ЩҠЩҠШІ ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ Symptoms ЩҲЩҺ Alerts
  • ШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Alert Definitions Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘ШөШ©
  • ШҘЩҗШ№ШҜШ§ШҜ Actions ЩҲЩҺ Notifications

ШіЩҗЩ„ШіЩҗЩ„Ш© Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ вҖ” Alert Chain

📚 Alert Flow

Metric Anomaly вҶ’ Symptom вҶ’ Alert Definition вҶ’ Alert вҶ’ Notification/Action

ComponentDefinitionШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш№ШұЩҠЩҒ
SymptomA condition that something is wrong (CPU > threshold)ШӯШ§Щ„Ш© ШӘЩҺШҜЩҸЩ„Щ‘ Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү Щ…ЩҸШҙЩғЩҗЩ„Ш©
Alert DefinitionCombination of symptoms + severity + recommendationsШӘЩҺШ№ШұЩҠЩҒ ЩҠЩҺШ¬Щ…ЩҺШ№ ШЈЩҺШ№ШұШ§Ш¶ + Ш®ЩҸШ·ЩҲШұШ©
AlertActive triggered alert instanceШӘЩҺЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ Щ…ЩҸЩҒЩҺШ№ЩҺЩ‘Щ„
ActionAutomated response (email, webhook, remediation)Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ¬Ш§ШЁШ© ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

Notification Plugins

  • Email (SMTP): ШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ ШӘЩҺЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ ШЁЩҗШ§Щ„ШЁЩҺШұЩҠШҜ
  • Webhook: ШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ Щ„ЩҗЩҖ Slack, Teams, ServiceNow
  • Log Forwarding: ШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ Щ„ЩҗЩҖ Syslog/Splunk
  • Remediation: ШӘЩҺЩҶЩҒЩҠШ° ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ Ш№ЩҗЩ„Ш§Ш¬ЩҠ ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҠ
🔬 Lab 22: Configuring Alerts

ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Alert Definition Щ…ЩҸШ®ЩҺШөЩҺЩ‘Шө Щ…ЩҺШ№ Symptom ЩҲЩҺ Notification.

Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ ШӘЩҺШ№ШұЩҠЩҒ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ вҖ” Alert Definition Components

ComponentRoleRequired?Ш§Щ„ШҜЩҺЩ‘ЩҲШұ
Symptom DefinitionCondition that triggers (threshold, event, property)Yes (1+)Ш§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШұШ· Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШӯЩҺЩҒЩҗЩ‘ШІ
RecommendationSuggested remediation stepsOptionalШ®ЩҸШ·ЩҲШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШҘЩҗШөЩ„Ш§Шӯ
ActionAutomated response (script, notification, power off)OptionalШ§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ¬Ш§ШЁШ© ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

ШЈЩҺЩҶЩҲШ§Ш№ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШ№ШұШ§Ш¶ вҖ” Symptom Types

TypeTriggerExampleЩ…ЩҗШ«Ш§Щ„
Metric/PropertyNumeric thresholdCPU > 90% for 10 minШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШ№Ш§Щ„ЩҗШ¬ > 90%
Message EventMessages from systemVM powered off unexpectedlyVM ШЈЩҸШәЩ„ЩҗЩӮ ШЁЩҗШҙЩҺЩғЩ„ ШәЩҺЩҠШұ Щ…ЩҸШӘЩҺЩҲЩҺЩӮЩҺЩ‘Ш№
FaultAvailability eventsHost connection lostЩҒЩҸЩӮЩҗШҜ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШӘЩҗЩ‘ШөШ§Щ„
LogsLog patternsError in syslogШ®ЩҺШ·ЩҺШЈ ЩҒЩҠ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш¬ЩҗЩ„Щ‘Ш§ШӘ

ШіЩҺЩҠШұ Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮ вҖ” Alert Creation Workflow

⚠️ Alert Definition Steps
  1. Name & Description
  2. Base Object Type (VM, Host, Cluster)
  3. Alert Impact: Health (ЩҒЩҺЩҲШұЩҠ) | Risk (ШЈЩҺЩҠЩ‘Ш§Щ…) | Efficiency (Ш·ЩҺЩҲЩҠЩ„ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺЩ…ЩҺШҜ)
  4. Criticality: Symptom-Based ШЈЩҺЩҲ Custom
  5. Add Symptoms (1+)
  6. Add Recommendations (optional)
  7. Add Actions (optional)
  8. Configure Notifications (Email/Webhook/SNMP)

Ш§Щ„ШҘЩҗШҙШ№Ш§ШұШ§ШӘ вҖ” Notification Methods

MethodConfigurationШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ
Email (SMTP)SMTP server, recipients, templateШ®Ш§ШҜЩҗЩ… SMTP ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШіШӘЩҺЩ„ЩҗЩ…ЩҠЩҶ
WebhookHTTP POST to ServiceNow, Slack, etc.POST Щ„ЩҗЩҶЩҗШёШ§Щ… Ш®Ш§ШұЩҗШ¬ЩҠ
SNMP Trapv1/v2c/v3 trap to NMStrap Щ„ЩҗЩҶЩҗШёШ§Щ… ШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© Ш§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩғШ©
REST APIExternal automation triggerШЈЩҺШӘЩ…ЩҺШӘШ© Ш®Ш§ШұЩҗШ¬ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

Automation Actions вҖ” Ш§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҗЩ‘Щ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

🧠 Available Actions

  • Power Off VM | Move VM (DRS) | Increase Resource
  • Run Script | Create Snapshot | Send Notification
  • Custom Action Ш№ЩҺШЁШұ REST API

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What is a Symptom in VCF Operations?

Correct: B

A Symptom is a defined condition that indicates something abnormal (metric exceeds threshold).

Q2. What is the correct alert flow?

Correct: B

The flow is: Metric Anomaly вҶ’ Symptom вҶ’ Alert Definition вҶ’ Alert вҶ’ Action.

Q3. Which notification methods does VCF Operations support?

Correct: B

VCF Operations supports Email, Webhook, Log Forwarding, and automated Remediation actions.

Module 18 · Health and Diagnostics

Ш§Щ„ШөЩҗЩ‘ШӯЩ‘Ш© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШҙШ®ЩҠШө

Health and Diagnostics

Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© ШөЩҗШӯЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҶШөЩ‘Ш© ЩҲЩҺШӘЩҺШҙШ®ЩҠШө Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШҙШ§ЩғЩҗЩ„ ШЁЩҗШіЩҸШұШ№Ш© Щ„ЩҗШ¶ЩҺЩ…Ш§ЩҶ Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗЩ…ШұШ§ШұЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„Ш®ЩҗШҜЩ…Ш©.

Learning Objectives
  • ЩҒЩҺЩҮЩ… Health Badges (Green/Yellow/Orange/Red)
  • Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ®ШҜШ§Щ… Root Cause Analysis
  • Capacity Planning ЩҲЩҺ What-If Analysis

Health Badges

BadgeIndicatesЩҠЩҺШҜЩҸЩ„Щ‘ Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү
HealthOverall object health (alerts, symptoms)ШөЩҗШӯЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШҙЩ‘Ш§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш©
WorkloadResource utilization levelЩ…ЩҸШіШӘЩҺЩҲЩү Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ®ШҜШ§Щ… Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ
Capacity RemainingTime to resource exhaustionШ§Щ„ЩҲЩҺЩӮШӘ ШӯЩҺШӘЩ‘Щү ЩҶЩҺЩҒШ§ШҜ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ

Root Cause Analysis

  • VCF Operations ЩҠЩҺШ№ШұЩҗШ¶ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ„Ш§ЩӮШ§ШӘ ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„ЩғШ§ШҰЩҗЩҶШ§ШӘ Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺШӘЩҺШЁЩҸЩ‘Ш№ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШіЩҺШЁЩҗЩ‘ШЁ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШіШ§ШіЩҠ
  • Object Relationships: VM вҶ’ Host вҶ’ Cluster вҶ’ Datastore вҶ’ Network
  • Impact/Contributor: Щ…ЩҺЩҶ ЩҠЩҺШӘЩҺШЈЩҺШ«ЩҺЩ‘Шұ ЩҲЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩҶ ЩҠЩҸШіЩҺШЁЩҗЩ‘ШЁ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШҙЩғЩҗЩ„Ш©

Capacity Planning

🧠 Capacity Analysis Features

  • Time Remaining: ЩғЩҺЩ… ШЁЩҺЩӮЩҠ ШӯЩҺШӘЩ‘Щү ЩҶЩҺЩҒШ§ШҜ CPU/RAM/Storage
  • What-If Analysis: Щ…Ш§Ш°Ш§ Щ„ЩҺЩҲ ШЈЩҺШ¶ЩҺЩҒЩҶШ§ 50 VM? вҖ” Щ…ЩҸШӯШ§ЩғШ§Ш©
  • Reclamation: ШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ idle/oversized VMs Щ„ЩҗШ§ШіШӘЩҗШ№Ш§ШҜШ© Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ
  • Right-Sizing: ШӘЩҺЩҲШөЩҠШ§ШӘ Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺЩӮЩ„ЩҠЩ„/ШІЩҗЩҠШ§ШҜШ© resources
🔬 Lab 23: Capacity Analysis

ШӘЩҺШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҺЩ‘Ш№Ш© ЩҲЩҺШӘЩҺЩҶЩҒЩҠШ° What-If scenario.

VCF Health Areas вҖ” Щ…ЩҺШ¬Ш§Щ„Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШөЩҗЩ‘ШӯЩ‘Ш©

AreaChecksШ§Щ„ЩҒЩҸШӯЩҲШөШ§ШӘ
Instance HealthManagement + Workload Domains statusШӯШ§Щ„Ш© Domains
Certificate HealthExpiry, validity, trust chainШ§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ЩҮШ§ШҜШ§ШӘ
ConnectivityCommunication between componentsШ§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШӘЩҗЩ‘ШөШ§Щ„
Password HealthExpiry and rotation complianceЩғЩҺЩ„ЩҗЩ…Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұЩҲШұ
Backup HealthComponent backup statusШ§Щ„ЩҶЩҸЩ‘ШіЩҺШ® Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШӯШӘЩҗЩҠШ§Ш·ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

ШЈЩҺШҜЩҲШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШҙШ®ЩҠШө вҖ” Diagnostic Tools

📚 Diagnostic Capabilities
  • Pre-Check: ЩҒЩҸШӯЩҲШөШ§ШӘ ЩӮЩҺШЁЩ„ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШұЩӮЩҠШ©
  • Health Check: ЩҒЩҸШӯЩҲШөШ§ШӘ ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш©
  • Connectivity Test: Ш§ЩҗШ®ШӘЩҗШЁШ§Шұ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШӘЩҗЩ‘ШөШ§Щ„ ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҸЩӮЩҺШҜ
  • Log Bundle: ШӘЩҺШ¬Щ…ЩҠШ№ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш¬ЩҗЩ„Щ‘Ш§ШӘ Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШҜЩҺЩ‘Ш№Щ…
  • Configuration Drift: ЩғЩҺШҙЩҒ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗЩҶШӯЩҗШұШ§ЩҒ

Diagnostic Findings вҖ” Щ…ЩҸШіШӘЩҺЩҲЩҠШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ШӘШ§ШҰЩҗШ¬

SeverityColorActionШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
CriticalRedImmediate resolutionШӯЩҺЩ„Щ‘ ЩҒЩҺЩҲШұЩҠ
WarningYellowAddress soonЩ…ЩҸШ№Ш§Щ„ЩҺШ¬Ш© ЩӮЩҺШұЩҠШЁШ©
InfoBlueNo action neededШЁЩҗШҜЩҲЩҶ ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
PassGreenCheck passedЩҶШ§Ш¬ЩҗШӯ

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What do Health Badges indicate?

Correct: B

Health Badges show Health (green-red), Workload utilization, and Capacity Remaining.

Q2. What does What-If Analysis provide?

Correct: B

What-If Analysis simulates adding/removing workloads to predict capacity impact.

Q3. What does Right-Sizing recommend?

Correct: B

Right-Sizing recommends adjusting VM CPU/RAM to match actual workload patterns.

Module 19 · Log Management and Storage Operations

ШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш¬ЩҗЩ„Щ‘Ш§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ

Log Management and Storage Operations

ШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© Щ…ЩҺШұЩғЩҺШІЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш¬ЩҗЩ„Щ‘Ш§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺЩ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ Щ„ЩҗШ§ЩғШӘЩҗШҙШ§ЩҒ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШҙШ§ЩғЩҗЩ„ ШЁЩҗШіЩҸШұШ№Ш©.

Learning Objectives
  • ШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Log Forwarding ЩҲЩҺ Log Analytics
  • Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© vSAN Performance ЩҲЩҺ Health
  • Storage Policies ЩҲЩҺ Reclamation

Log Management

  • Log Collection: Ш¬ЩҺЩ…Ш№ ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҠ Щ…ЩҗЩҶ ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ VCF
  • Log Analytics: ШЁЩҺШӯШ« ЩҲЩҺЩҒЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҗШұШ© ШЁЩҗЩҖ structured queries
  • Log Forwarding: ШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ Щ„ЩҗЩҖ Syslog, Splunk, ELK
  • Content Packs: ШӘЩҺШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„ Ш®Ш§ШөЩ‘ ШЁЩҗЩҖ vCenter, NSX, vSAN

Storage Operations

FeatureFunctionШ§Щ„ЩҲЩҺШёЩҠЩҒШ©
vSAN HealthReal-time health checks for vSANЩҒЩҸШӯЩҲШөШ§ШӘ ШөЩҗШӯЩ‘Ш© vSAN Ш§Щ„ШўЩҶЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©
Storage PoliciesDefine protection/performance levelsШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ Щ…ЩҸШіШӘЩҺЩҲЩҠШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӯЩҗЩ…Ш§ЩҠШ© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШЈЩҺШҜШ§ШЎ
ReclamationIdentify orphaned/stale VMDKsШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ ШЈЩҺЩӮШұШ§Шө VM ЩҠЩҺШӘЩҠЩ…Ш©
Capacity ForecastPredict when storage runs outШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶЩҺШЁЩҸЩ‘ШӨ ШЁЩҗЩҶЩҺЩҒШ§ШҜ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ
🔬 Lab 24: Configuring Log Forwarding

ШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Log Forwarding ШҘЩҗЩ„Щү Syslog server Ш®Ш§ШұЩҗШ¬ЩҠ.

VCF Operations for Logs вҖ” Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш¬ЩҗЩ„Щ‘Ш§ШӘ

FeatureDescriptionШ§Щ„ЩҲЩҺШөЩҒ
Log CollectionCentralized syslog + app log collectionШ¬ЩҺЩ…Ш№ Щ…ЩҺШұЩғЩҺШІЩҠ
Log SearchFull-text search with filtersШЁЩҺШӯШ« ЩҶЩҺШөЩ‘ЩҠ
Log AlertsSymptom-based alerts on log patternsШӘЩҺЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ ШЁЩҗШЈЩҺЩҶЩ…Ш§Ш·
Log ForwardingForward to SIEM (Splunk, ELK)ШҘЩҗШ№Ш§ШҜШ© ШӘЩҺЩҲШ¬ЩҠЩҮ

Storage Operations вҖ” Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ

📚 Storage Monitoring
  • Capacity: Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш№Ш© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶЩҺШЁЩҸЩ‘ШӨ ШЁЩҗШ§Щ„Ш§ЩҗЩ…ШӘЩҗЩ„Ш§ШЎ
  • Performance: IOPS, Latency, Throughput Щ„ЩҗЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Datastore
  • vSAN Health: Disk Groups, Resync status
  • Policy Compliance: Ш§ЩҗЩ…ШӘЩҗШ«Ш§Щ„ VMs Щ„ЩҗШіЩҗЩҠШ§ШіШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ
  • Reclaimable: ШӘЩҺШ®ШІЩҠЩҶ ЩӮШ§ШЁЩҗЩ„ Щ„ЩҗЩ„Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШұШҜШ§ШҜ (orphans, snapshots)

Network Operations вҖ” Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩғШ©

AreaMonitoringШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ©
NSX HealthManager, Controller, Edge statusШӯШ§Щ„Ш© Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ
Flow MonitoringE-W and N-S traffic analysisШӘЩҺШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұЩҲШұ
Micro-segmentationDFW rule hitsЩҒЩҺШ№Ш§Щ„ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ЩӮЩҺЩҲШ§Ш№ЩҗШҜ
LatencyNetwork latency between VMsШІЩҺЩ…ЩҶ Ш§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҗШ¬Ш§ШЁШ©
TopologyVisual network mapШ®ЩҺШұЩҠШ·Ш© ШЁЩҺШөЩҺШұЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What are Content Packs?

Correct: B

Content Packs provide pre-built dashboards and queries specific to products like vCenter, NSX, vSAN.

Q2. What does Storage Reclamation identify?

Correct: B

Storage Reclamation identifies orphaned/stale VMDKs and snapshots that can be safely deleted to recover space.

Q3. Where can logs be forwarded to?

Correct: B

Logs can be forwarded to external systems like Syslog, Splunk, and ELK.

Module 20 · Centralized Monitoring and Operations

Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШұЩғЩҺШІЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ

Centralized Monitoring and Operations

ШұЩҺШЁШ· ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҒШ§ЩҮЩҠЩ… Щ…ЩҺШ№Ш§ЩӢ Щ„ЩҗШЁЩҗЩҶШ§ШЎ Day-2 Operations Щ…ЩҸШӘЩҺЩғШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш© ШӘЩҸШәЩҺШ·Щ‘ЩҠ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШөЩҗЩ‘ЩҠШ§ЩҶШ© ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯШіЩҠЩҶ.

Learning Objectives
  • ШӘЩҺШөЩ…ЩҠЩ… Monitoring Strategy ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш©
  • Integration Щ…ЩҺШ№ ШЈЩҺШҜЩҲШ§ШӘ Ш®Ш§ШұЩҗШ¬ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© (ITSM, Slack, PagerDuty)
  • ШЈЩҺЩҒШ¶ЩҺЩ„ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩ…Ш§ШұЩҺШіШ§ШӘ Щ„ЩҗЩҖ Day-2 Operations
  • Lifecycle Management ЩҲЩҺ Updates

Monitoring Strategy

  • Proactive: ML-based predictions ЩӮЩҺШЁЩ„ ШӯЩҸШҜЩҲШ« Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШҙЩғЩҗЩ„Ш©
  • Reactive: ШіЩҸШұШ№Ш© Ш§ЩғШӘЩҗШҙШ§ЩҒ ЩҲЩҺШӯЩҺЩ„Щ‘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺШҙШ§ЩғЩҗЩ„ Ш№ЩҗЩҶШҜ ШӯЩҸШҜЩҲШ«ЩҮШ§
  • Preventive: ШөЩҗЩҠШ§ЩҶШ© ШҜЩҺЩҲШұЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© (patches, health checks, compliance)

Integration Щ…ЩҺШ№ ШЈЩҺЩҶШёЩҗЩ…Ш© Ш®Ш§ШұЩҗШ¬ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

SystemIntegration MethodШ·ЩҺШұЩҠЩӮШ© Ш§Щ„ШұЩҺЩ‘ШЁШ·
ServiceNowBidirectional incident managementШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© ШӯЩҺЩҲШ§ШҜЩҗШ« Ш«ЩҸЩҶШ§ШҰЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„Ш§ШӘЩҗЩ‘Ш¬Ш§ЩҮ
Slack/TeamsWebhook notificationsШҘЩҗШҙШ№Ш§ШұШ§ШӘ Ш№ЩҺШЁШұ Webhook
PagerDutyAlert escalationШӘЩҺШөШ№ЩҠШҜ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ
SplunkLog and metric forwardingШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҗЩ‘Ш¬ЩҗЩ„Щ‘Ш§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі

Day-2 Operations Best Practices

🧠 Operational Excellence Checklist

  • Monitor: Dashboards + Alerts + Notifications Щ…ЩҸЩҒЩҺШ№ЩҺЩ‘Щ„Ш©
  • Maintain: Patches + Updates + Certificate rotation Щ…ЩҸЩҶШӘЩҺШёЩҺЩ…Ш©
  • Optimize: Right-sizing + Reclamation + Capacity Planning ШҙЩҺЩҮШұЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш§ЩӢ
  • Comply: Compliance checks + Configuration drift detection
  • Automate: Self-healing + Automated remediation ШӯЩҺЩҠШ«ЩҸ ШЈЩҺЩ…ЩғЩҺЩҶ
  • Document: Runbooks + Change logs + Knowledge base

Lifecycle Management

  • VCF Lifecycle Manager: ШӘЩҺШұЩӮЩҠШ© ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ ШЁЩҗШӘЩҺШұШӘЩҠШЁ ШөЩҺШӯЩҠШӯ
  • Pre-check: ЩҒЩҺШӯШө ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„ ЩӮЩҺШЁЩ„ ШЈЩҺЩҠЩ‘ ШӘЩҺШұЩӮЩҠШ©
  • Rolling Updates: ШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШ« ШЁЩҗШҜЩҲЩҶ downtime
  • Rollback: ШҘЩҗЩ…ЩғШ§ЩҶЩҠЩ‘Ш© Ш§Щ„ШұЩҸЩ‘Ш¬ЩҲШ№ ЩҒЩҠ ШӯШ§Щ„ ЩҒЩҺШҙЩҺЩ„
🔬 Lab 25: Configuring Notifications

ШұЩҺШЁШ· Email ЩҲЩҺ Webhook notifications Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ.

🔬 Lab 26: Health Check and Compliance

ШӘЩҺЩҶЩҒЩҠШ° ЩҒЩҺШӯШө ШөЩҗШӯЩ‘Ш© ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„ ЩҲЩҺ Compliance audit.

Service Discovery вҖ” Ш§ЩҗЩғШӘЩҗШҙШ§ЩҒ Ш§Щ„Ш®ЩҗШҜЩ…Ш§ШӘ

MethodDiscoversЩҠЩҺЩғШӘЩҺШҙЩҗЩҒ
OS ProcessRunning processes, services, open portsШ§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҶШ§ЩҒЩҗШ°
App MappingDependencies between servicesШ§Щ„Ш§ЩҗШ№ШӘЩҗЩ…Ш§ШҜЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ
Network ConnectionTCP/UDP connections between workloadsШ§ЩҗШӘЩҗЩ‘ШөШ§Щ„Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩғШ©

Application Monitoring вҖ” Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш·ШЁЩҠЩӮШ§ШӘ

🧠 Monitoring Levels

  • Infrastructure: VM resources (CPU, Memory, Disk, Network)
  • OS Level: Guest metrics (processes, services, file systems)
  • Application: Response time, error rate, throughput
  • Dependency: Service mesh and inter-app relationships

Telegraf Agent вҖ” ЩҲЩҺЩғЩҠЩ„ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ©

FeatureDescriptionШ§Щ„ЩҲЩҺШөЩҒ
DeploymentLightweight agent inside VMsЩҲЩҺЩғЩҠЩ„ Ш®ЩҺЩҒЩҠЩҒ
Plugins200+ input plugins (MySQL, Apache, Docker)200+ Щ…ЩҸЩ„ШӯЩҺЩӮ
MetricsOS and app-level metricsЩ…ЩҺЩӮШ§ЩҠЩҠШі Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҗЩ‘ШёШ§Щ… ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш·ШЁЩҠЩӮ
PushSends to VCF Operations for analysisЩҠЩҸШұШіЩҗЩ„ Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„

End-to-End Monitoring вҖ” Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© Ш§Щ„ШҙЩ‘Ш§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш©

💡 Full Stack Visibility
  • ШұЩҸШӨЩҠШ© ШҙШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„Ш©: Infrastructure вҶ’ OS вҶ’ Application
  • ЩғЩҺШҙЩҒ ШӘЩҗЩ„ЩӮШ§ШҰЩҠ Щ„ЩҗЩ„Ш§ЩҗШ№ШӘЩҗЩ…Ш§ШҜЩҠЩ‘Ш§ШӘ
  • ШӘЩҺЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ Ш°ЩҺЩғЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш© ШӘЩҸШұШ§Ш№ЩҠ ШіЩҗЩҠШ§ЩӮ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш·ШЁЩҠЩӮ Ш§Щ„ЩғШ§Щ…ЩҗЩ„
  • Root Cause Analysis Ш№ЩҺШЁШұ ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Ш§Щ„Ш·ЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩӮШ§ШӘ

✅ Knowledge Check

Q1. What integration method is used for ServiceNow?

Correct: B

ServiceNow integration is bidirectional вҖ” alerts create incidents, and closures sync back.

Q2. What does VCF Lifecycle Manager do?

Correct: B

VCF Lifecycle Manager handles upgrading all components in the correct dependency order.

Q3. What are the key pillars of Day-2 Operations?

Correct: B

Day-2 Operations encompass: Monitor, Maintain, Optimize, Comply, Automate, and Document.

Q4. What type of Monitoring uses ML-based predictions?

Correct: B

Proactive monitoring uses Machine Learning predictions to detect issues before they occur.

Practice · Operational Toolkit

ШөЩҸЩҶШҜЩҲЩӮ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШҜЩҲШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШҙШәЩҠЩ„ЩҠ

Operational Toolkit вҖ” Quick Reference Runbooks

ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎШ§ШӘ ШӘЩҺШҙШәЩҠЩ„ЩҠЩ‘Ш© ШіЩҺШұЩҠШ№Ш© Щ„ЩҗШЈЩҺЩғШ«ЩҺШұ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҮШ§Щ…Щ‘ ШҙЩҸЩҠЩҲШ№Ш§ЩӢ ЩҒЩҠ ШЁЩҺЩҠШҰШ© VCF. Ш§ЩҗШіШӘЩҺШ®ШҜЩҗЩ… ЩғЩҺЩ…ЩҺШұШ¬ЩҗШ№ ШіЩҺШұЩҠШ№ ШЈЩҺШ«ЩҶШ§ШЎ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„ Ш§Щ„ЩҠЩҺЩҲЩ…ЩҠ.

🔧 Runbook 1: ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Region Ш¬ЩҺШҜЩҠШҜШ©

StepActionШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
1Provider Portal вҶ’ Infrastructure вҶ’ Regions вҶ’ AddЩҒЩҺШӘШӯ ШөЩҺЩҒШӯШ© ШҘЩҗШ¶Ш§ЩҒШ© Region
2Set name, description, geo locationШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ Ш§Щ„Ш§ШіЩ… ЩҲЩҺШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҲЩӮЩҗШ№
3Select VCF Instance(s) to associateШұЩҺШЁШ· VCF Instance
4Define Availability ZonesШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ Щ…ЩҺЩҶШ§Ш·ЩҗЩӮ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҲЩҒЩ‘Шұ
5Assign compute/storage resourcesШӘЩҺШ®ШөЩҠШө Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ
6Configure Provider NetworkingШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩғШ§ШӘ

🔧 Runbook 2: ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Щ…ЩҸЩҶЩҺШёЩҺЩ‘Щ…Ш© Ш¬ЩҺШҜЩҠШҜШ©

StepActionШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
1Provider Portal вҶ’ Organizations вҶ’ CreateШЁЩҺШҜШЎ ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Щ…ЩҸЩҶЩҺШёЩҺЩ‘Щ…Ш©
2Select type: All Apps / VM Apps / PCOШ§ЩҗШ®ШӘЩҗЩҠШ§Шұ Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ЩҲШ№
3Assign Region(s)ШӘЩҺШ®ШөЩҠШө Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҶШ§Ш·ЩҗЩӮ
4Set Org Admin userШӘЩҺШ№ЩҠЩҠЩҶ Щ…ЩҸШҜЩҠШұ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩҶЩҺШёЩҺЩ‘Щ…Ш©
5Configure Resource QuotasШӘЩҺШӯШҜЩҠШҜ ШӯЩҸШҜЩҲШҜ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ШұЩҗШҜ
6Enable Feature FlagsШӘЩҺЩ…ЩғЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҠШІШ§ШӘ

🔧 Runbook 3: ЩҶЩҺШҙШұ VM Щ…ЩҗЩҶ Catalog

StepActionШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
1Organization Portal вҶ’ CatalogЩҒЩҺШӘШӯ Ш§Щ„ЩғЩҺШӘШ§Щ„ЩҲШ¬
2Select Catalog Item (Blueprint)Ш§ЩҗШ®ШӘЩҗЩҠШ§Шұ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҸЩҶШөЩҸШұ
3Fill in request form (name, size, network)Щ…ЩҗЩ„ШЎ Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘Щ…ЩҲШ°ЩҺШ¬
4Submit request вҶ’ wait for approval (if policy)ШҘЩҗШұШіШ§Щ„ Ш§Щ„Ш·ЩҺЩ‘Щ„ЩҺШЁ
5Monitor deployment in Deployments viewЩ…ЩҸШӘШ§ШЁЩҺШ№Ш© Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ШҙШұ

🔧 Runbook 4: ШӘЩҺШҙШ®ЩҠШө Alert ЩҒЩҠ VCF Operations

StepActionШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
1VCF Operations вҶ’ Alerts вҶ’ Active AlertsЩҒЩҺШӘШӯ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҶШЁЩҠЩҮШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ЩҶЩҺЩ‘ШҙЩҗШ·Ш©
2Click alert вҶ’ view SymptomsШ№ЩҺШұШ¶ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШ№ШұШ§Ш¶
3Check Related Objects (Root Cause)ШӘЩҺШӯЩҺЩӮЩҸЩ‘ЩӮ Щ…ЩҗЩҶ Ш§Щ„ШіЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺШЁ Ш§Щ„Ш¬ЩҺШ°ШұЩҠ
4View RecommendationsШ№ЩҺШұШ¶ Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ЩҲШөЩҠШ§ШӘ
5Take action / acknowledge / cancelШ§ШӘЩҗЩ‘Ш®Ш§Ш° ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ

🔧 Runbook 5: Capacity Planning

StepActionШ§Щ„ШҘЩҗШ¬ШұШ§ШЎ
1VCF Operations вҶ’ Capacity вҶ’ Time RemainingШ№ЩҺШұШ¶ Ш§Щ„ЩҲЩҺЩӮШӘ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШӘЩҺШЁЩҺЩӮЩ‘ЩҠ
2Review CPU, RAM, Storage trendsЩ…ЩҸШұШ§Ш¬ЩҺШ№Ш© Ш§Щ„Ш§ШӘЩҗЩ‘Ш¬Ш§ЩҮШ§ШӘ
3Run What-If: add workloadsЩ…ЩҸШӯШ§ЩғШ§Ш© ШҘЩҗШ¶Ш§ЩҒШ© ШЈЩҺШӯЩ…Ш§Щ„
4Check Reclamation recommendationsШ№ЩҺШұШ¶ ШӘЩҺЩҲШөЩҠШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„Ш§ШіШӘЩҗШұШҜШ§ШҜ
5Right-Size oversized VMsШӘЩҺШ№ШҜЩҠЩ„ ШЈЩҺШӯШ¬Ш§Щ… VMs
Practice · Real-World Scenarios

ШіЩҺЩҠЩҶШ§ШұЩҠЩҲЩҮШ§ШӘ ЩҲШ§ЩӮЩҗШ№ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©

Real-World Scenarios

ШіЩҺЩҠЩҶШ§ШұЩҠЩҲЩҮШ§ШӘ Щ…ЩҗЩҶ ШЁЩҺЩҠШҰШ§ШӘ ШҘЩҗЩҶШӘШ§Ш¬ ШӯЩҺЩӮЩҠЩӮЩҠЩ‘Ш© Щ„ЩҗШӘЩҺШ·ШЁЩҠЩӮ Щ…Ш§ ШӘЩҺШ№ЩҺЩ„ЩҺЩ‘Щ…ШӘЩҮ ЩҒЩҠ Щ…ЩҺЩҲШ§ЩӮЩҗЩҒ ЩҲШ§ЩӮЩҗШ№ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш©.

Scenario 1: Multi-Region Deployment

📚 Context

ШҙЩҺШұЩҗЩғШ© Щ„ЩҺШҜЩҺЩҠЩҮШ§ Щ…ЩҺШұЩғЩҺШІШ§ ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ (Dubai, Riyadh). ШӘЩҸШұЩҠШҜ ШЁЩҗЩҶШ§ШЎ private cloud Щ…ЩҺШ№ failover ШЁЩҺЩҠЩҶ Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҺЩҲЩӮЩҗШ№ЩҺЩҠЩҶ.

🧠 Solution Approach

  1. ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Fleet ЩҲШ§ШӯЩҗШҜ Щ…ЩҺШ№ VCF Operations + Automation
  2. ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Region Щ„ЩҗЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Щ…ЩҲЩӮЩҗШ№ (Region-Dubai, Region-Riyadh)
  3. ШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Availability Zones ЩҒЩҠ ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Region
  4. ШҘЩҗШ№ШҜШ§ШҜ Provider Gateway + BGP ЩҒЩҠ ЩғЩҸЩ„ЩҗЩ‘ Region
  5. ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ Щ…ЩҸЩҶЩҺШёЩҺЩ‘Щ…Ш§ШӘ Щ…ЩҺШ№ access Щ„ЩҗЩҖ ЩғЩҗЩ„Ш§ Ш§Щ„ЩҖ Regions
  6. Blueprints Щ…ЩҺШ№ multi-AZ placement Щ„ЩҗЩ„ЩҖ failover

Scenario 2: Self-Service Platform for Dev Teams

📚 Context

ЩҒЩҺШұЩҠЩӮ ШӘЩҺШ·ЩҲЩҠШұ ЩҠЩҺШӯШӘШ§Ш¬ 50+ environments ШЈЩҸШіШЁЩҲШ№ЩҗЩҠЩ‘Ш§ЩӢ. DBA load Ш№Ш§Щ„ЩҠ Щ„ЩҗЩӮЩҺЩҲШ§Ш№ЩҗШҜ Ш§Щ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШ§ЩҶШ§ШӘ. Ш·ЩҺЩ„ЩҺШЁШ§ШӘ ШЁЩҺШ·ЩҠШҰШ© Ш№ЩҺШЁШұ ITSM.

🧠 Solution Approach

  1. ШҘЩҗЩҶШҙШ§ШЎ "All Apps" Organization Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш·ЩҲЩҠШұ
  2. ШӘЩҺШөЩ…ЩҠЩ… Blueprints Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШҰШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШҙЩ‘Ш§ШҰЩҗШ№Ш© (Web+DB, Microservices)
  3. ЩҶЩҺШҙШұ ЩғЩҺЩҖ Catalog Items Щ…ЩҺШ№ Custom Forms
  4. ШӘЩҺЩҒШ№ЩҠЩ„ Data Services Manager Щ„ЩҗЩҖ self-service DBs
  5. ШӘЩҺШ№ЩҠЩҠЩҶ Lease Policy (7 days) Щ„ЩҗЩ…ЩҺЩҶШ№ sprawl
  6. ШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҠЩҶ Approval Policy Щ„ЩҗЩ„ШЁЩҺЩҠШҰШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ЩғЩҺШЁЩҠШұШ© ЩҒЩҺЩӮЩҺШ·

Scenario 3: Performance Troubleshooting

📚 Context

ШӘЩҺШ·ШЁЩҠЩӮ ШҘЩҗЩҶШӘШ§Ш¬ ЩҠЩҸШ№Ш§ЩҶЩҠ Щ…ЩҗЩҶ ШЁЩҸШ·ШЎ Щ…ЩҸЩҒШ§Ш¬ЩҗШҰ. Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШіШӘЩҺШ®ШҜЩҗЩ…ЩҲЩҶ ЩҠЩҺШҙШӘЩҺЩғЩҲЩҶ. Щ„Ш§ ЩҠЩҲШ¬ЩҺШҜ ШӘЩҺШәЩҠЩҠШұ ЩҲШ§Ш¶ЩҗШӯ.

🧠 Troubleshooting Steps

  1. Check Health Badge Щ„ЩҗЩ„ЩҖ VM вҖ” ШЈЩҺШӯЩ…ЩҺШұ?
  2. View Active Alerts вҖ” Щ…Ш§ ЩҮЩҠ Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШ№ШұШ§Ш¶?
  3. Object Relations вҖ” ЩҮЩҺЩ„ Host ШЈЩҺЩҲ Datastore Щ…ЩҸШӘЩҺШЈЩҺШ«ЩҗЩ‘Шұ?
  4. Metrics Analysis вҖ” CPU/RAM/Disk contention?
  5. Check Noisy Neighbors вҖ” VMs ШЈЩҸШ®ШұЩү Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү ЩҶЩҺЩҒШі Host?
  6. Right-Size / Migrate ШЁЩҗЩҶШ§ШЎЩӢ Ш№ЩҺЩ„Щү Ш§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘ШӯЩ„ЩҠЩ„

VCF 9 AOP Quick Reference Cheat Sheet

⚡ VCF Architecture at a Glance

LayerComponentsШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҸЩғЩҺЩҲЩҗЩ‘ЩҶШ§ШӘ
Fleet LevelVCF Operations + VCF AutomationШ§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШұШ§ЩӮЩҺШЁШ© + Ш§Щ„ШЈЩҺШӘЩ…ЩҺШӘШ©
Instance LevelManagement Domain + Workload DomainsЩҶЩҗШ·Ш§ЩӮ Ш§Щ„ШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© + ЩҶЩҗШ·Ш§ЩӮШ§ШӘ Ш§Щ„Ш№ЩҺЩ…ЩҺЩ„
MSPIdentity, Certificate, Lifecycle MgmtШ®ЩҗШҜЩ…Ш§ШӘ Ш§Щ„ШҘЩҗШҜШ§ШұШ© Ш§Щ„Щ…ЩҸШҙШӘЩҺШұЩҺЩғШ©
ComputevSphere + ESXi + VMs + TKGШ§Щ„ШӯЩҺЩҲШіЩҺШЁШ©
StoragevSAN + NFS + iSCSIШ§Щ„ШӘЩҺЩ‘Ш®ШІЩҠЩҶ
NetworkNSX + Edge Clusters + VPCsШ§Щ„ШҙЩҺЩ‘ШЁЩҺЩғШ§ШӘ

vcf-cli task listList running tasks
vcf-cli certificate listList certificate status
vcf-cli upgrade checkCheck available upgrades

🔬 Lab 1: Case Study

Module 01 вҖ” Course Introduction

Case Study: Rainpole Learning Organization

Rainpole, a leading education services provider, is on a strategic journey to expand its learning platform capabilities to support the future growth of the organization. As part of this transformation, Rainpole recognizes the critical need for a robust, agile, and scalable private cloud infrastructure to support its learning Lab infrastructure and training delivery with hands-on labs for cloud service providers.

Their current infrastructure is built on traditional vSphere, which is reaching its limits. The current infrastructure lacks the flexibility and automation needed for rapid innovation. As a result, Rainpole is evaluating VMware Cloud Foundation for its next-generation data center that has the potential to be highly available, agile, and secure.

This lab environment and the accompanying document are meant to act as a learning and teaching tool to gain expertise on the VCF Automation and VCF Operations components. When these components work together, they provide an industry-leading environment to build, automate, consume, and operate your own private cloud.

Proof of Concept

As a proof of concept, the CIO has decided to build a sample private cloud using VCF to set up the infrastructure and use VCF Automation on top to build the private cloud. The cloud acts as a playground environment for the learning team to run virtual machines as a classroom teaching aid as well as for learning content development. VCF Operations is used to monitor and troubleshoot the environment.

Automate Learning Goals

This lab environment and the accompanying document are meant to serve as a learning and teaching tool to gain expertise on the VCF Automation and VCF Operations components. When these components work together, they provide an industry-leading environment to build, automate, consume, and operate your own private cloud.

Participants acquire the following primary VCF Automation skills from this exercise:

  • As a provider admin, create a region to utilize the underlying pool of infrastructure resources that include compute, storage, and network.
  • Create an organization called learning_org that acts as the proof-of-concept environment where the learning team deploys their test workloads.
  • Configure the networking components that enable the learning_org workloads with East-West and North-South traffic. These tasks include importing the edge cluster, creating a provider gateway, and creating the IP spaces for the organization.
  • Set up a virtual private cloud as a sandbox to deploy workloads for learning_org users.
  • Create content libraries at the provider and organization levels.
  • Create projects and namespaces for deploying workloads.
  • Manage users and roles within the organization.
  • Manage blueprints and catalogs.
  • Manage orchestrator workflows.
  • Deploy VM workloads using the catalog option for novice users and IaaS options for advanced users.

Operate Learning Goals

This lab environment and the accompanying document are meant to act as a learning and teaching tool to gain expertise on the VCF Automation and VCF Operations components. When these components work together, they provide an industry-leading environment to build, automate, consume, and operate your own private cloud.

Participants acquire the following VCF Operations skills from this exercise:

  • As an operator, you navigate through the key areas in the VCF Operations UI.
  • Create a custom view to fetch VM Configuration details.
  • Create a custom report to get daily and weekly updates on a list of VMs.
  • Create custom dashboards for the NOC team to continuously monitor key metrics.
  • Create custom symptoms and alerts for the NOC team to monitor the critical workloads.
  • Use VCF Health and Diagnostics to monitor the VCF private cloud.
  • Review the key capabilities of VCF Operations for logs.
  • Monitor storage operations to proactively observe storage behavior to identify and address issues, and optimize performance.
  • Monitor network operations to proactively observe network behavior to identify and address issues, optimize performance, and ensure security.
  • Configure Service discovery and Application Monitoring to ensure that applications are resilient and performant.

🔬 Lab 4: Configuring an Identity Provider

Module 04 вҖ” Provider Identity Management

Task 1: (Optional) Log In to the VCF Automation Provider

  1. On the Google Chrome bookmarks bar, right-click VCF Automation and select Open in new incognito window.
    • If the Your connection is not private message appears, click Advanced and click Proceed to sa-vaa01.vcf.sddc.local(unsafe).
      • Under Organization name, enter system
    • Log in to the VCF Automation Provider Management portal.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
  2. Leave the VCF Automation Provider Management Portal open for the next task.

Task 2: Configure an Open LDAP Connection

  1. On the Provider Management page, click Identity Providers under Administration.
  2. Click the LDAP tab.
  3. Click CONFIGURE.
  4. On the Edit LDAP page, configure the Open LDAP settings. Option Action Server dc.vclass.local port Base Distinguished Name dc=vclass,dc=local Connector type Open LDAP Use SSL Turn on the toggle to enable. Authentication Method Leave Simple selected. User Name administrator@vclass.local Password VMware1!
  5. Click SAVE.
  6. In the Trust Certificate window, click TRUST SELECTED to trust the certificate.

Task 3: Test the Connection

  1. On the Provider Management page, ensure that Identity Providers under Administration is selected.
  2. Click TEST. The Test LDAP window appears.
    • Enter VMware1! as the password.
    • Click TEST.
  3. Verify that the Test LDAP window appears as Connected with a green tick.
  4. Click X to close the Test LDAP window.
  5. Click SYNC. The Synchronize LDAP window appears.
    • Click SYNC. The Synchronization with LDAP has started message appears.
    • Click Recent Tasks to review the synchronized System LDAP
  6. Click Recent Tasks.
    • Verify that the Synchronized System LDAP entry status shows as Succeeded.

🔬 Lab 6: Creating a Region

  4. From the NSX Local Manager drop-down menu, select sa-wld01-nsxt-vip.vcf.sddc.local.

  5. Click Storage Classes.

🔬 Lab 9: Configuring Provider Networking

Module 07 вҖ” Provider Networking

Task 1: (Optional) Log In to the VCF Automation Provider

  1. On the Google Chrome bookmarks bar, right-click VCF Automation and select Open in new incognito window.
    • If the Your connection is not private message appears, click Advanced and click Proceed to sa-vaa01.vcf.sddc.local(unsafe).
      • Under Organization name, enter system
    • Log in to the VCF Automation Provider Management Portal. From the first drop-down menu, select Log in with local account.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
    • Leave the VCF Automation Provider Management Portal open for the next task.

Task 2: Verify Edge Cluster Import

  1. Click Networking under Infrastructure.
  2. On the Networking page, click Edge Clusters.
  3. Click SYNC.
  4. Verify that the sa-wld-cl01 edge cluster is available.

Task 3: Create an IP Space

  1. Click Networking under Infrastructure.
  2. Click the IP Spaces tab.
  3. Click NEW. The Create IP Space wizard appears.
  4. Specify details for Configure General Settings.
    • In the Name text box, enter region1_IP_Space
    • From the region drop-down menu, select region1.
    • Click NEXT.
  5. Specify the IP Block and External Reachability.
    • In the IP Block text box, enter 10.10.10.32/27
      • Click + ADD to add the IP range.
    • In the External Reachability text box, enter 0.0.0.0/0
      • Click + ADD to add the IP range.
    • Click NEXT.
  6. Specify Default Quota Settings values.
    • For Number of Single IPs, select the Unlimited checkbox.
    • For Number of CIDRs, select the Unlimited checkbox.
    • For Maximum Subnet Size, select the No Restriction checkbox.
    • Click NEXT.
  7. Verify the settings in the Review and Complete pane.
    • Click CREATE.
  8. Verify that the IP space is created.

Task 4: Create a Provider Gateway

  1. Click Networking under Infrastructure.
  2. Click the Provider Gateways tab.
  3. Click NEW to create a provider gateway.
  4. Specify details for Configure General Settings.
    • In the Name text box, enter region1_pg
    • From the Region drop-down menu, select region1.
      • Click NEXT.
  5. Under Select T0 Gateway, select the sa-wld01-t0-01 checkbox.
    • Click NEXT.
  6. Under Associated IP Spaces, select the region1_IP_Space checkbox.
    • Click NEXT.
  7. Verify the settings in the Review and Complete pane and click CREATE.
  8. Verify that region1_pg is created successfully.

Task 5: Set Up Organization Networking

  1. Click Organizations under Infrastructure.
  2. Click Learning_Org. The Learning_Org page appears.
  3. Select Networking.
  4. Click EDIT to edit the log name.
    • In the Log Name text box, enter learning
    • Click SAVE.
  5. Under Regional Networking, click NEW.
  6. From the Select Region drop-down menu, select region1.
    • Click NEXT.
  7. Under Select Provider Gateway, select the region1_pg checkbox.
    • Click NEXT.
  8. Specify the details for the Select Edge Cluster section.
    • Select Select a specific Edge Cluster.
    • Select sa-wld01-cl01.
    • Click NEXT.
  9. In the Review and Complete section, click CREATE.

🔬 Lab 13: Managing Users and Roles

Module 10 вҖ” Organization Management

Task 1: Use the VCF Automation System LDAP Service

  1. On the Google Chrome bookmarks bar, right-click VCF Automation and select Open in new incognito window.
    • If the Your connection is not private message appears, click Advanced and click Proceed to sa-vaa01.vcf.sddc.local(unsafe).
      • Under Organization name, enter system
    • Log in to the VCF Automation Provider Management Portal. From the first drop-down menu, select Log in with local account.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
  2. Click Organizations under Infrastructure.
  3. Click Learning_Org.
  4. On the Learning_Org page, click LAUNCH ORGANIZATION PORTAL.
    • The Learning_Org organization portal is launched.
  5. Click Administer.
    • Click Identity Providers under Connections.
  6. Edit the LDAP settings.
    • Click the LDAP tab.
    • Click CONFIGURE. The Edit LDAP Options window appears.
    • Select VCF Automation system LDAP Service.
    • In the Distinguished name for the organizational unit text box, enter ou=learning,dc=vclass,dc=local
  7. Click SAVE.

Task 2: Import Users into Learning_Org

  1. Click Access Control.
  2. Import the learning-admin user.
    • Click IMPORT USERS. The Import Users window appears.
    • Place your cursor in the Search field.
    • Enter learning-admin and click Search.
    • Select the learning-admin checkbox.
    • From the Assign Role drop-down menu, select Organization Administrator.
    • Click SAVE.
  3. Import learning-user and learning-aduser users.
    • Click IMPORT USERS. The Import Users window appears.
    • Place your cursor in the Search field.
    • Enter learning-user and click Search.
    • Select the learning-user checkbox.
    • Enter learning-aduser and click Search.
    • Select the learning-aduser checkbox.
    • From the Assign Role drop-down menu, select Organization User.

  1. Select the CCI_Supervisor_Namespace_1 component in the design canvas.
  2. Click the Properties tab in the right pane.

    • Explore the Topology tab as your deployment progresses.

🔬 Lab 21: Navigating the VCF Operations UI

Task 1: Log In to the VCF Operations Administration UI

  1. Connect to the administration UI of the VCF Operations instance.
    • In Chrome, open a new browser tab, and select Infrastructure > VMware Cloud Foundation Operations Administration on the bookmarks toolbar. The VCF Operations Administration page appears.
  2. Log in to the VCF Operations admin UI.
    • User name: admin
    • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
  3. Click System Status in the navigation pane to verify the cluster status. Q1. What is the system status in the VCF Operations Admin UI? A1. The VCF Operations cluster is online. The System Status pane shows the cluster status, fleet management, high availability, and continuous availability configuration under Configure Availability. You can configure high availability and continuous availability. Q2. How can you enable high availability on this cluster? Why is the Activate HA option unavailable? A2. To enable high availability on a cluster, you need at least two nodes. Only one node exists in the VCF Operations cluster.
  4. In the navigation pane, click Support. The Support pane shows various logs. You can generate the support bundles for VCF Operations and Cloud Proxy from this pane.
  5. From the User drop-down menu, select Log Out.
  6. Close the VMware Cloud Foundation Operations Administration tab.

Task 2: Navigate Pages in the VCF Operations Product UI

  1. Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
    • In Chrome, open a new browser tab and select VCF OPS on the bookmarks toolbar.
    • In the Login Method drop-down menu, leave Local Account selected.
    • Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
      • The VCF Operations home page appears. The home page includes an Overview and Launchpad page. The Overview dashboard provides a high-level view of the objects that compose your private cloud environment. You can also view a list of all your data centers, including inventory information about how many clusters, hosts, and virtual machines are running in each of your data centers. You can narrow down by the areas of appliances health and management, as well as workload operations.
  2. Click the Launchpad tab. The Launchpad page appears, which offers an overview of the key areas.
  3. Scroll down the Launchpad page to view the remaining key areas. Q1. What are the names of the key areas? A1. Fleet Management, Operations, Self-service Private Cloud, Virtualized Infrastructure, and Public Cloud.
  4. View the esx-1.vcf.sddc.local object from the Inventory page.
    • Click Inventory in the navigation pane.

    • Expand esx-1.vcf.sddc.local. This example shows how you can identify related environments and can view the objects in the vSphere inventory. You can expand the other environments listed on the left side to explore objects in those environments.
  5. Review the contents of the Dashboards page.
    • Click Infrastructure Operations > Dashboards & Reports > Dashboards in the navigation pane.
    • View the contents of Overview on the Dashboards page. The Overview page is divided into six broad categories: Availability, Configuration, Inventory, Performance, Capacity, and Cost.
  6. Review the contents of the Views page.
    • Click Views in the navigation pane.
    • View the contents of Overview on the Views page. The Overview page is divided into six broad categories: Availability, Capacity, Configuration, Inventory, Performance, and Compliance.
  7. Review the contents of the Reports page.
    • Click Reports in the navigation pane.
    • View the contents of the Reports Templates.

Task 3: Use the Search Functionality to Find Objects

  1. Search for the esx-2.vcf.sddc.local host.

    • From the header, enter ubuntu-01a in the search box. The user interface searches for object names that contain the ubuntu-01a string.
    • Click ubuntu-01a. The content pane shows the Summary page for the ubuntu-01a object. Q1. Which VMware Tools version is running on ubuntu-01a VM? A1. Tools version 12.3.5 runs on ubuntu-01a. Q2. Does the ubuntu-01a VM have any active alerts? A2. No. Q3. What values are provided for Time Remaining and Capacity Remaining? A3. Time remaining is greater than 1 year and capacity remaining is 55%. The values might vary depending on your lab. Q4. What values are provided for CPU Usage and Free Memory in the Utilization pane? A4. Values vary depending on the current resource usage.

Task 4: Use Dashboards and Topology to Navigate the Environment

  1. Click Infrastructure Operations > Dashboards & Reports > Dashboards in the navigation pane. Home appears in the content pane. The Home page provides broad categories, including Availability, Configuration, Inventory, Performance, Capacity, and Cost.
  2. Expand Inventory. The dashboards available in Inventory are categorized into four logical groups.
  3. Click vSphere Compute Inventory. The vSphere Compute Inventory dashboard appears. You can use the vSphere Compute Inventory dashboard to browse through the topology of your vSphere compute inventory, which includes information related to vSphere World, vCenter, data center, clusters, hosts, virtual machines, properties, and metrics.
  4. Double-click EDU-dc01 to view the vSphere objects in the object hierarchy.
  5. Review the object hierarchy by selecting different objects and verify that every time you change the selection, widgets are repopulated with data from the newly selected object. Widgets are often configured to interact with each other. Selecting an object in one widget populates the other widgets with data for the selected object.
  6. You use topology to display relationship with clusters, hosts, and VMs objects.
    • Search for the data center named EDU-dc01.
    • Enter EDU-dc01 in the Search text box.
    • Click EDU-dc01. The content pane shows the data for the EDU-dc01 object.
  7. Click the Topology tab.
    • View the relationship of EDU-dc01 with other objects in the inventory.

🔬 Lab 22: Creating a Custom View

Module 15 вҖ” Dashboards and Views

Task 1: Create a View that Provides the VM Configuration Details

  1. Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
    • In Chrome, select VCF OPS on the bookmarks toolbar.
    • In the Login Method drop-down menu, leave Local Account selected.
    • Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
  2. Click Infrastructure Operations > Dashboards & Reports in the navigation pane.
  3. Select Views.
  4. Click + Create to create a view that displays the resource information for a virtual machine.
  5. Click List from View Types.
  6. On the Name & Configuration tab, configure the viewвҖҷs name and description. Option Action Name Enter VM Configuration Details in the text box. Description Enter Provides CPU, memory, and disk information for the VMs in the text box.
  7. Edit view presentation settings.
    • Expand Settings to reveal additional view settings.
    • Enter 25 in the Items per page text box.
    • Click NEXT.

Task 2: Define the Data to Include in the VM Configuration Details

  1. On the Data tab, configure the viewвҖҷs subject.
    • Enter virtual machine in the Add Subject drop-down menu.
    • Select Virtual Machine from the result list.
  2. Add multiple metrics to the Data panel.
    • Expand Metrics in the metrics picker.
    • Expand CPU.
    • Drag Effective limit (MHz) to the Data panel. The Data panel has the Drag the data to include in the view message.
  3. Add the virtual machine Memory metric to the Data panel.
    • Expand Memory.
    • Drag Total Capacity (KB) to the Data panel.
  4. Add two virtual machine Guest File System metrics to the Data panel.
    • Expand Guest File System.
    • Drag Total Capacity (GB) to the Data panel.
    • Drag Utilization (GB) to the Data panel.
  5. Arrange the metrics in the Data panel exactly as listed. You can rearrange the following metrics by dragging one above the other: CPU Effective limit (MHz) Memory | Total Capacity (KB) Guest File System | Total Capacity (GB) Guest File System | Utilization (GB)
  6. Configure the CPU|Effective Limit metric.
    • Select the CPU|Effective Limit metric in the Data panel.
    • Enter CPU Capacity in the Metric label text box. The metric label name changes in the Data panel.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select GHz.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select Descending.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp.
  7. Configure the Memory|Total Capacity Limit metric.
    • Select the Memory|Total Capacity metric in the Data panel.
    • Enter Memory Capacity in the Metric label text box.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select GB.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select None.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp.
  8. Configure the Guest File System|Total Capacity metric.
    • Select Guest File System|Total Capacity in the Data panel.
    • Enter File System Capacity in the Metric label text box.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select GB.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select Descending.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp.
  9. Configure the Guest File System|Utilization metric.
    • Select the fourth metric in the Data panel, Guest File System|Utilization.
    • Enter File System Usage in the Metric label text box.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select Auto.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select Descending.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp. Stay on the same page for the next task.

  1. From the Preview source drop-down menu, select Select preview source. The Select an Object dialog box appears.
  2. From the Select an Object screen, expand VCF Instances > EDU > EDU > sa-m01- vc01.vcf.sddc.local > EDU-dc01.
  3. Select the EDU-cl01 cluster and click OK.
  4. Click the refresh button in the preview source pane.
  5. View the information in your view.
  6. Verify that the metric labels, units, and sort order look correct.
  7. In the Preview source panel, verify that the CPU Capacity and Timestamp columns are positioned to the left of the Memory Capacity columns.
  8. Click NEXT.
  9. Leave the default values for the 3 - Time Settings section and click NEXT.
  10. Leave the default values for the 4 - Filter section and click NEXT.

Task 4: Add a Summary Row to the VM Configuration Details View

  1. On the Summary tab, click ADD SUMMARY.
  2. In the Configuration panel, configure the summary settings.
    • Enter Average in the Summary title text box.
    • From the Aggregation drop-down menu, select Average.
  3. Click the Refresh icon in the upper-right corner to refresh the Preview source panel.

  5. Click CREATE.

Task 3: Configure a Widget Interaction in the vSphere Metrics

  1. Edit the vSphere Metrics dashboard.

  2. Create an interaction between the Metric Picker widget and the Environment Overview widget. a. Click SHOW INTERACTIONS. Two types of icons are available: receiver and connector. The blue circle represents Objects: The blue circle with a circle and dot inside represents an Incoming Object interaction (receiver). In contrast, the blue circle with a circle and arrow inside represents an Outgoing Object interaction (connector). The orange circle represents Metrics: The orange circle with a circle and dot inside represents an Incoming Metric interaction (receiver). The orange circle with a circle and arrow inside represents an Outgoing Metric interaction (connector). b. In the Environment Overview widget, click the object connector icon and drag the pointer to the object receiver icon in the Metric Picker widget.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT
  3. Create an interaction between the Metric Picker widget and the Metric Chart widget.
    • In the Metric Picket widget, click the metric connector icon and drag the pointer from this icon to the metric receiver icon.
    • Click SAVE. The Metric Picker and Metric Chart widgets do not display any information until you interact with the widgets.
  4. Test the widget interactions. a. In the Environment Overview widget, click the centos-01a virtual machine. If centos-01a is not available, you can choose any other virtual machine. The dashboard view and VM names in your lab environment might be different from the screenshot. b. Verify that the Metric Picker widget displays the Favorites, Metrics, and Properties sections. c. In the Metric Picker widget, expand Metrics > CPU and double-click Usage (%). d. Verify that the metric chart appears in the Metric Chart widget. Task 3: Create the TestDev Policy for Objects in the TestDev Group

  1. Click Infrastructure Operations > Configurations in the navigation pane.
  2. In the Policies section, click Policy Definition.
  3. Click ADD. The Create New Policy wizard appears.
  4. Configure the general settings for the new, custom policy. Option Action Name Enter TestDev Policy in the text box. Description Enter Assigned to the custom group named TestDevGroup in the text box. Inherit From Select Base Settings from the drop-down menu.
  5. Click CREATE POLICY.
  6. Click Capacity to configure the capacity settings.
  7. Change the Time Remaining element and Workload element settings for the virtual machines (VMs) in the TestDev policy.
    • Locate the Capacity Thresholds and Metrics configurations section. Click the downward double arrow next to Capacity Thresholds and Metrics to expand this section.
    • Select vCenter > Cluster Compute Resource.
    • Click the lock icon to enable editing and modify the Time Remaining element. Clicking the lock icon enables you to override the default settings.
    • Drag the red marker to the left to set the Critical Time Remaining to 60 (unit is days).
    • Click the lock icon to enable editing and modify the Workload element.
    • Set the red marker to 96.
  8. Click SAVE to save your policy.
  9. Apply the policy to TestDev Group.
    • Click Groups and Objects.
    • Select the TestDev Group checkbox.
  10. Click SAVE to save your policy.

Task 4: Create the VMScale Policy for Objects in the VMScale Group

  4. Click CREATE POLICY.
  5. Configure the newly created policy settings.
    • Click Capacity.
  6. Change the Time Remaining element and Workload element settings for the virtual machines (VMs) in the VMScaleGroup.

      • Select vCenter > Cluster Compute Resource.
    • Click the lock icon to enable editing and modify the Time Remaining element. Clicking the lock icon enables you to override the default settings.
    • Drag the red marker to the left to set the Critical Time Remaining to 70 (unit is days).
    • Click the lock icon to enable editing and modify the Workload element.
    • Set the orange marker to 85.
    • Click SAVE.
  7. Apply the policy to VMScale Group.
    • Click Groups and Objects.
    • Select the VMScale Group checkbox.
    • Click SAVE.

Task 6: Export a Policy

  1. Click Infrastructure Operations > Configurations in the navigation pane.
  2. Click Policy Definition.
  3. Select TestDev Policy from the policies list.
  4. Click the Manage button (ellipsis icon) and select Export. The policy .xml file downloads to the Downloads folder on your Console (student01) machine. In larger environments, you can reuse exported policies across different VCF Operations instances to save time by avoiding re-creating policies.

Task 2: Create a Symptom Definition to Check for Medium CPU

  1. Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
    • In Chrome, select VCF OPS on the bookmarks toolbar.

    • Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!

  5. Select Virtual Machine as the base object type. The virtual machine metrics appear.

    • Enter 30 in the Numeric Value text box.

  8. Click SAVE.
  9. Verify that the VM Medium CPU Demand symptom appears in the Symptom Definitions list. If your symptom does not appear on the first page of the list, you can use the search text box in the top-right corner to find your symptom. You can also create a filter based on the Defined By column. The user defines the search for alerts.

🔬 Lab 27: Creating Custom Alert Definitions

Module 17 вҖ” Symptoms, Alerts, and Actions

Task 1: Configure a Virtual Machine Alert

  1. Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
    • In Chrome, select VCF OPS on the bookmarks toolbar.
    • In the Login Method drop-down menu, leave Local Account selected.
    • Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
      • User name: admin
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
  2. Start the Alert Definition Workspace wizard.
    • Click Infrastructure Operations > Configurations in the navigation pane.
    • In the Alerts section, click Alert Definitions.
    • Click ADD. The Create Alert Definition wizard appears.
  3. Configure the alert name and description. Every alert definition has a name and an optional description. Use names that are meaningful in your environment and create a description that provides helpful information to the user.
    • Enter VM CPU Demand in the Name text box.
    • Enter Check for high VM CPU Demand in the Description text box.
  4. Set the base object type to virtual machine.
    • Enter virtual machine in the Base Object Type search box.
    • Select Virtual Machine from the list.
  5. Configure advanced settings.
    • Expand Advanced Settings.
    • From the Impact drop-down menu, select Health.
    • From the Criticality drop-down menu, select Immediate.
    • From the Alert Type & Subtype drop-down menu, select Application: Performance.
    • Enter 1 in the Wait Cycle text box.
    • Enter 180 in the Cancel Cycle text box.
  6. Click NEXT.
  7. Add a symptom to the alert definition. An alert definition includes one or more symptom definitions.
    • In the Defined On drop-down menu, leave Self selected.
    • Click the Symptoms tab.
    • In the Select Symptom drop-down menu, leave Metric/Property selected.
    • Enter VM High in the Quick Filter box.
    • From the Symptom list, select VM High CPU Demand and drag it to the Drag a symptom in to create a new symptom set area in the center pane.
  8. Click NEXT.
  9. Add recommendations to the alert definition.
    • Enter Check the applications running on the virtual machines in the cluster to determine whether high CPU workload is an expected behavior in the Quick Filter box.
    • Drag the Check the applications running on the virtual machines in the cluster to determine whether high CPU workload is an expected behavior recommendation to the Drop recommendation here section. When you add multiple recommendations, the first recommendation takes higher priority than those added after it.
    • Click NEXT.
  10. Select a policy for the alert.
    • Select the TestDev Policy checkbox.
  11. Click CREATE.

Task 2: Test the Custom Alert Definition

  1. Start an SSH session to connect to the ubuntu-01a VM.
    • On the Ubuntu taskbar on the student desktop, click the Remmina icon.
    • Double-click ubuntu-01a. You are connected to ubuntu-01a as user vmware. If you are prompted to sign in to the ubuntu-01a VM, enter VMware123!VMware123! as the password.
  2. Run the for i in 1 2 3 4; do while : ; do : ; done & done script on the ubuntu-01a virtual machine. In your lab environment, the process IDs are expected to be different than those in the screenshot.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT
  3. Review the CPU utilization for ubuntu-01a.
    • Navigate back to the VCF OPS Admin tab in the Chrome browser.
    • Enter ubuntu-01a in the search box. The ubuntu-01a object page appears.
  4. Click the Alerts tab.
  5. Verify that the alert is triggered. a. Click the Alerts tab next to Symptoms. b. From the Group By drop-down menu, select Criticality. c. Expand the arrow next to the Immediate section. d. Verify that the alert VM CPU Demand appears in the list. The CPU metric data and the triggered CPU demand-related alert can take up to 15 minutes to reflect in the VCF Operations console.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT
  6. View the alert details.
    • Click VM CPU Demand. Information for the VM CPU Demand alert appears to the right.
    • Review the alert information, recommendations, and symptoms details.

Task 3: Manage Generated Alerts

  1. Return to the VCF OPS Chrome browser tab.
  2. Click Infrastructure Operations > Alerts in the navigation pane.
  3. From the Group By drop-down menu, select Definition.
  4. Select an active alert.
    • From the All Filters drop-down menu, select Status > Active. Only active alerts in each group appear.
    • Expand the VM CPU Demand alert.
    • Click VM CPU Demand.
  5. Review the options available from the Actions drop-down menu.
  6. Suspend alerts for 2 hours.
    • From the Actions drop-down menu, click Suspend. The Confirmation dialog box appears.
    • Enter 120
    • Click OK. Alerts can also be disabled when you group them by definition.
  7. List only the suspended alerts on the All Alerts page.
    • From the All Filters drop-down menu, click CLEAR ALL to clear existing filters.
    • Click VIEW MORE FILTERS.
    • From the Control State drop-down menu, select Suspended.
    • Click APPLY. Only suspended alerts are listed.
  8. Cancel an active alert.
    • Expand VM CPU Demand and select the VM CPU Demand active alert that you just suspended.
    • From the Actions drop-down menu, click Cancel Alert.
    • Click YES in the Cancel Groups Alerts dialog box.
    • If the Info Selected group alerts were canceled message appears, click OK.
  9. Verify that the status of the canceled alert is now inactive. a. From the All Filters drop-down menu, select CLEAR ALL to clear any existing filters. b. From the All Filters drop-down menu, select Status > Inactive. c. Click APPLY. The alert that you just canceled should appear in the list. If you did not see the recently cancelled alert, click the Load More + button to display more cancelled alerts.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT
  10. Expand VM CPU Demand definition category, and then select the checkbox for the VM CPU Demand alert that you just canceled.
  11. Delete a canceled alert.
    • From the Actions drop-down menu, select Delete Canceled Alerts.
    • Click Yes.
    • Click OK.
  12. Verify that the alert is removed from the list. If you still could see the cancelled VM CPU Demand alert, you can try refresh the browser to reload the inactive alert list.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT
  13. Terminate the CPU loop check script to reduce the ubuntu-01a CPU utilization. a. From the student console, click the Remmina icon to return to the ubuntu-01a SSH session. b. Record the four process IDs. __________ c. Run the kill <process ID> command to stop the CPU check process. The script should look like kill 3009. The process ID is expected to be different in your lab environment. d. Run the kill <process ID> command to terminate all four CPU check processes.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT
  14. Check the CPU utilization on ubuntu-01a.
    • From the ubuntu-01a command-line interface, run the top command. The CPU utilization should be close to 0%.
    • (Optional) If the CPU utilization in the top command result does not appear close to 0%, press Ctrl+C to stop the top command and run top again to show the updated CPU utilization.
    • Press Ctrl+C to stop the top command.

Task 4: Create a Log File Plug-In Instance

  1. Click Infrastructure Operations > Configurations in the navigation pane.
  2. In the Alerts section, click Outbound Settings.
  3. Click ADD. The Create New Outbound Instance wizard opens.
  4. Select Log File Plugin from the Plugin Type drop-down menu.
  5. Enter EDU Log File Plugin as the instance name.
  6. Enter /tmp/logfiles as the alert output folder. The log file is placed in the /tmp/logfiles directory on the VCF Operations node.

  8. Click OK.
  9. Click SAVE to save the plug-in configuration.
  10. Verify that the Log File Plugin appears in the Outbound Instances list and a gray check mark appears in the status column.

The VCF Automation Orchestrator client provides more detailed information about the vCenter inventory than the vSphere Client. The vm folder is not visible in the vSphere Client. When a vCenter instance is created, the Datacenters folder is created. When a data center is created in vCenter, the vm folder is created. The host, datastore, and network folders are also created simultaneously.

Task 2: Define the Data to Include in the VM Configuration Details

  1. On the Data tab, configure the viewвҖҷs subject.
    • Enter virtual machine in the Add Subject drop-down menu.
    • Select Virtual Machine from the result list.
  2. Add multiple metrics to the Data panel.
    • Expand Metrics in the metrics picker.
    • Expand CPU.
    • Drag Effective limit (MHz) to the Data panel. The Data panel has the Drag the data to include in the view message.
  3. Add the virtual machine Memory metric to the Data panel.
    • Expand Memory.
    • Drag Total Capacity (KB) to the Data panel.
  4. Add two virtual machine Guest File System metrics to the Data panel.
    • Expand Guest File System.
    • Drag Total Capacity (GB) to the Data panel.
    • Drag Utilization (GB) to the Data panel.
  5. Arrange the metrics in the Data panel exactly as listed. You can rearrange the following metrics by dragging one above the other: CPU Effective limit (MHz) Memory | Total Capacity (KB) Guest File System | Total Capacity (GB) Guest File System | Utilization (GB)
  6. Configure the CPU|Effective Limit metric.
    • Select the CPU|Effective Limit metric in the Data panel.
    • Enter CPU Capacity in the Metric label text box. The metric label name changes in the Data panel.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select GHz.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select Descending.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp.
  7. Configure the Memory|Total Capacity Limit metric.
    • Select the Memory|Total Capacity metric in the Data panel.
    • Enter Memory Capacity in the Metric label text box.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select GB.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select None.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp.
  8. Configure the Guest File System|Total Capacity metric.
    • Select Guest File System|Total Capacity in the Data panel.
    • Enter File System Capacity in the Metric label text box.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select GB.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select Descending.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp.
  9. Configure the Guest File System|Utilization metric.
    • Select the fourth metric in the Data panel, Guest File System|Utilization.
    • Enter File System Usage in the Metric label text box.
    • From the Units drop-down menu, select Auto.
    • From the Sort order drop-down menu, select Descending.
    • From the first Transformation drop-down menu, select Last.
    • From the second Transformation drop-down menu, select Absolute Timestamp. Stay on the same page for the next task.

The blue circle represents Objects: The blue circle with a circle and dot inside represents an Incoming Object interaction (receiver). In contrast, the blue circle with a circle and arrow inside represents an Outgoing Object interaction (connector). The orange circle represents Metrics: The orange circle with a circle and dot inside represents an Incoming Metric interaction (receiver). The orange circle with a circle and arrow inside represents an Outgoing Metric interaction (connector). b. In the Environment Overview widget, click the object connector icon and drag the pointer to the object receiver icon in the Metric Picker widget.

Task 2: Create a Symptom Definition to Check for Medium CPU

  1. Log in to the VCF Operations UI.

      • User name: admin

    • In the first drop-down menu, verify that Static Threshold remains selected.
    • Enter VM Medium CPU Demand in the Name text box.
    • In the Condition drop-down menu, verify that > remains selected.
    • Enter 30 in the Numeric Value text box.
    • From the Criticality drop-down menu, select Warning.
    • Expand Advanced Settings.
    • In the Wait Cycle text box, enter 1. Setting a value of 1 enables the alert to trigger after one polling cycle or 5 minutes.
    • In the Cancel Cycle text box, enter 5.
  8. Click SAVE.
  9. Verify that the VM Medium CPU Demand symptom appears in the Symptom Definitions list. If your symptom does not appear on the first page of the list, you can use the search text box in the top-right corner to find your symptom. You can also create a filter based on the Defined By column. The user defines the search for alerts.

Task 1: Configure a Virtual Machine Alert

  1. Log in to the VCF Operations UI.
    • In Chrome, select VCF OPS on the bookmarks toolbar.

  2. Start the Alert Definition Workspace wizard.
    • Click Infrastructure Operations > Configurations in the navigation pane.
    • In the Alerts section, click Alert Definitions.
    • Click ADD. The Create Alert Definition wizard appears.
  3. Configure the alert name and description. Every alert definition has a name and an optional description. Use names that are meaningful in your environment and create a description that provides helpful information to the user.
    • Enter VM CPU Demand in the Name text box.
    • Enter Check for high VM CPU Demand in the Description text box.

    • Drag the Check the applications running on the virtual machines in the cluster to determine whether high CPU workload is an expected behavior recommendation to the Drop recommendation here section. When you add multiple recommendations, the first recommendation takes higher priority than those added after it.
    • Click NEXT.
  10. Select a policy for the alert.
    • Select the TestDev Policy checkbox.
  11. Click CREATE.
