Task 3: View the vSphere Widgets

  1. Click Infrastructure > VCF Health in the navigation pane.
  2. Click EDU from the VCF Instances list and click sa-wld01 from the VCF Domains list. The sa-wld01 domain dashboard opens.
  3. Locate the vCenter Instances section and click View Details. The sa-wld01-vc01.vcf.sddc.local vCenter Health dashboard opens.
  4. Locate the Connectivity widget and click View Details. The Appliance Health page opens. On the Appliance Health page, you can view the following sections: Connectivity: VCF Operations monitors the vCenter connectivity across key parameters, such as Ping, UI Service, and API Service, to ensure its availability. You can interact with each chart to modify the time intervals and view connectivity counts. Utilization: This section provides insights into the vCenter performance from a scaling perspective. It tracks various utilization parameters and compares them against predefined thresholds. When a parameter reaches its threshold, the widget offers scaling recommendations and guidance on how to increase capacity to maintain optimal performance. Services: This section displays the status of critical vCenter services, indicating whether each service is started or stopped and whether it is healthy or experiencing issues. Monitoring these services ensures that all necessary vCenter components are functioning properly.
  5. Click sa-wld01-vc01.vcf.sddc.local from the navigation path to return to the sa-wld01-vc01 vCenter domain health dashboard.
  6. Under Capabilities, locate the VM Operations widget and click View Details. The Virtual Machine Operations page opens. The Virtual Machine Operations page provides information on all operations related to VMs, including actions such as power, create, delete, and hardware modifications. Monitoring this information ensures smooth VM management.
  7. Click sa-wld01-vc01.vcf.sddc.local from the navigation path to return to the sa-wld01-vc01 vCenter domain health dashboard.
  8. Under Capabilities, locate the vMotion widget and click View Details. The vMotion page opens. The vMotion page provides a detailed overview of vMotion events, categorized into successful and failed migrations.
  9. Click sa-wld01-vc01.vcf.sddc.local from the navigation path to return to the sa-wld01-vc01 vCenter domain health dashboard.
  10. Under Capabilities, locate the Snapshots widget and click View Details. The Snapshots page opens. The Snapshots page shows the status of snapshot operations, whether they are successful, failed, or in progress.
  11. Click sa-wld01-vc01.vcf.sddc.local from the navigation path to return to the sa-wld01-vc01 vCenter domain health dashboard.
  12. Under Components, locate the vSAN Cluster section and click View Dashboard. The vSAN Health dashboard opens. The vSAN Health dashboard shows the status of the vSAN clusters in your environment. You can view the properties, number of alerts, and the associated alerts of each vSAN cluster.
  13. Select the vSAN Cluster(EDU-cl01) row from the vSAN Clusters widget.
  14. Click vSAN Cluster(EDU-cl01) because it redirects you to the vSAN Cluster(EDU-cl01) details page.
  15. From the Alert List widget, click the After one additional host failure, vSAN Cluster will not have enough resources to rebuild all objects alert. The vSAN Cluster(EDU-cl01) page opens and automatically shows the details for the selected alert. You can view the symptoms and recommendations for this alert, or go to Troubleshoot Workbench to further troubleshoot this alert. You might not see the same alerts in your lab environment. If you do not see the alert specified in this step, you can click any other alert to enter the corresponding VM details page and review the alert information.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT

Task 4: Review the Diagnostic Findings

  1. Click Diagnostic Findings.
  2. On the Diagnostic Findings page, review the diagnostics information that appears on the Active Findings tab.
  3. From the active findings list, expand any finding and review the finding details. Each diagnostic finding includes information, such as a related Broadcom knowledge base (KB) article number, severity, finding type/subtype, product area, description, number of objects affected, VCF components, and so on. You can use the information from the finding description to investigate issues or apply best practices. You can use the Broadcom KB article number to read the article in the Broadcom knowledge base portal at https://www.broadcom.com/support/knowledgebase.
  4. Click the Findings Catalog tab.
  5. Review the Filters settings. You can use the Filters to help you narrow the search and locate the findings relevant to what you want to review or resolve.
  6. Review the findings on the Findings Catalog tab. The findings under Findings Catalog show all the findings available to your VCF environment. These findings might not have any actively affected objects or indicate any active issue. They simply provide information to optimize your environment or prevent future issues. At any point, if any object in your environment enters a potentially faulty state, the relevant diagnostic findings under Findings Catalog becomes active and appears under Active Findings. In a production environment, you must ensure the connectivity between components in your environment. The networking port required between VCF Operations and endpoints in ESX, vCenter, NSX, and SDDC Manager is SSL 443. For Log Assist, the connection is between the cloud proxy and the respective component, not from the cluster node. For VCF Operations for logs, the required port is 9543. The minimum bandwidth is 200 KB/s.

Task 3: Create Log Events

  1. Log in to the vSphere Client.
    • In Chrome, open a new browser tab and click the Workload Domain > vSphere Client (sa-wld01-vc01) bookmark.
    • Log in to the vSphere Client:
      • User name: administrator@vsphere.local
      • Password: VMware123!VMware123!
  2. In the vSphere Client, click the Hosts and Clusters icon in the left navigation pane.
  3. Enable SSH client access through the firewall to create firewall log entries for esx-
  4. vcf.sddc.local.
    • In the left navigation pane, select sa-wld01-vc01.vcf.sddc.local > sa-wld01-DC > sa- wld01-cl01 > esx-5.vcf.sddc.local.
    • In the right pane, click the Configure tab.
    • In the navigation pane on the Configure tab, select System > Firewall.
    • On the Firewall page, click EDIT.
    • In the Edit Security Profile dialog box, click the SECURE SHELL tab.
    • Select the SSH Client check box.
    • Click OK.
  5. Disallow SSH client access through the firewall.
    • On the Firewall page, click EDIT.
    • In the Edit Security Profile dialog box, click the SECURE SHELL tab.
    • Deselect the SSH Client check box.
    • Click OK.
  6. Repeat step 3 - 4 to create firewall log entries for esx-6.vcf.sddc.local.

Task 4: Review and Analyze Logs with Simple Queries

  1. Return to the VCF Operations console browser tab, then navigate to Infrastructure Operations > Analyze.
  2. Search for events from the last hour that contain the word "firewall."
    • In the Search logs for text containing search field, enter firewall.
    • For the log history selection, select 1H.
    • Click the Search (resembles a magnifying glass) button. The log stream should display all log entries related to firewall changes.
  3. Create a filter to find firewall events for the esx-5 host only.
    • Under the search field, click + ADD FILTER.
    • Locate the first keyword text field, delete text (the default keyword), type host, and then select hostname from the first drop-down menu.
    • Verify that contains is selected from the second drop-down menu.
    • Enter esx-5 in the text box next to contains.
    • Click the Search button. The log stream should now display only log entries from esx-5.vcf.sddc.local.
  4. Create a filter to find firewall events that contain the word "enable" on the esx-5 host.
    • Click + ADD FILTER.
    • Verify that text is selected from the first drop-down menu.
    • Select contains from the second drop-down menu.
    • Enter enable in the text box next to contains.
    • Click the Search button. The log stream should now be further filtered. You can see firewall events on esx-
  5. vcf.sddc.local with the keyword "enable."

The Agent Type column should show Product Managed Agent, if the Telegraf agent was installed from the VCF Operations console UI. The Last Operation Status column should show Install Success. Because of the design of the lab environment, the Telegraf agent installation only works on ubuntu-02a. The other VMs either have restrictive setups or were deployed as functional components of the VCF environment. Only the ubuntu-02a VM was designed to accept the Telegraf agent installation.
    • вҡ пёҸ IMPORTANT

Task 3: Configure a Custom Remote Check

  1. Click Workload Operations > Applications in the navigation pane.
  2. Click Manage Telegraf Agents.
  3. Add custom monitoring for the ubuntu-01a VM.
    • Expand the ubuntu-02a VM.
    • Click the Manage icon (vertical ellipsis icon) for UDP Check and click Add.
    • Complete the following custom UDP Check configurations. Display Name: Enter Custom UDP Check Address: Enter google.com Send: Enter Ping google.com Expect: Enter 200 Timeout: Leave blank. Read Timeout: Leave blank.
    • Click Save.
  4. Examine the custom UDP check status.
    • Expand the ubuntu-02a VM.
    • Expand UDP Check. The added custom UDP check appears. 192 Answer Key Lab 21 Navigating the VCF Operations UI Q1. What is the system status in the VCF Operations Admin UI? A1. The VCF Operations cluster is online. The System Status pane shows the cluster status, fleet management, high availability, and continuous availability configuration under Configure Availability. You can configure high availability and continuous availability. Q2. How can you enable high availability on this cluster? Why is the Activate HA option unavailable? A2. To enable high availability on a cluster, you need at least two nodes. Only one node exists in the VCF Operations cluster. Q1. What are the names of the key areas? A1. Fleet Management, Operations, Self-service Private Cloud, Virtualized Infrastructure, and Public Cloud. Q1. Which VMware Tools version is running on ubuntu-01a VM? A1. Tools version 12.3.5 runs on ubuntu-01a. Q2. Does the ubuntu-01a VM have any active alerts? A2. No. Q3. What values are provided for Time Remaining and Capacity Remaining? A3. Time remaining is greater than 1 year and capacity remaining is 55%. The values might vary depending on your lab. Q4. What values are provided for CPU Usage and Free Memory in the Utilization pane? A4. Values vary depending on the current resource usage. Lab 30 Monitoring Storage Operations Q1. What is the storage capacity listed for the EDU-CL01-ds-vsan01 vSAN data store?
  5. 52 TB. A1. The actual usage might be different in your lab environment. Q2. How many hosts are listed? A2. Four. Q3. How many vSAN disk groups does the cluster contain? A3. Four. Q4. Including all hosts, how many total capacity disks does the cluster contain? A4. Eight. Each host contributes one cache device and two capacity devices. Q5. What is the total capacity and usage of the data store? Is it the same as the value that appears in the vSphere Client? A5. The total capacity is 3.52 TB. The usage should be the same as that displayed in the vSphere Client. Q6. How many hosts are using this data store? A6. Four, including esx-1, esx-2, esx-3, and esx-4. Q7. How many disk groups do you see under EDU-cl01-ds-vsan01? A7. Four. Q8. How many disks are grouped under each disk group? A8. Three, including one cache disk and two capacity disks. Q9. What is the storage capacity listed for the sa-wld01-cl01-vsan01 vSAN data store?
  6. 56 TB. A9. The actual usage might be different in your lab environment. Q10. How many hosts are listed? A10. Four. Q11. How many vSAN disk groups does the cluster contain? A11. Four. Q12. Including all hosts, how many total capacity disks does the cluster contain? A12. Eight. Each host contributes one cache device and two capacity devices. Q13. What is the total capacity and usage of the data store? Is it the same as the value recorded from the vSphere Client? A13. The total capacity is 1.56 TB. The usage should be the same as the value that appears in the vSphere Client. Q14. How many hosts are using this data store? A14. Four, including esx-5, esx-6, esx-7, and esx-8. Q15. How many disk groups do you see under sa-wld01-cl01-vsan01? A15. Four. Q16. How many disks are grouped under each disk group? A16. Three, including one cache disk and two capacity disks. Q1. How many data stores can you see on the Storage Operations page and what is their type? A1. Two data stores. vSAN OSA. Q2. How much disk space is usable? What is the used percentage? What is the recommended disk size based on the current used percentage? A2.
  7. 64 TB is usable. The used percentage and recommended size might be different in different lab vApps.
